O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and practice of the medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is completely unknown to everyone, the science has perished and diminished, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in books by ancient authors which have been handled by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And this is the cause of errors and false beliefs, and understanding has been closed off and knowledge has moved away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, as well as the other instruments of the work with the addition of explanation and preparation, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who practices medicine must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they may know thoroughly the members and their forms, connections, and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and arteries, and their number, and movement and repose, and the origin of their issuance.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates said that "name is much with name, and little with the work," and the same applies to the art of handicraft.[Translating "li nos" as "the name" and "l'uevre" as "the work"]
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book, that he who is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, should be careful not to fall into error and not to kill men; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula in a woman's neck and cut the arteries of the neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he removed a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they operated on him, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see one other physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break also had a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound with splints, and left no bandage on the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it at all; and it remained so until the leg was completely swollen and the foot became lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had unbound it, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But still the gangrene had already set in the leg, and I could not heal it; and the gangrene continued to spread through the limb until the whole member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who lanced a hardened abscess, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his handling.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron if one cannot completely remove what is corrupt in that place.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: namely, tasks where there is risk in multiple ways; and I will show in each section of this book where there is danger and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary that you be careful to avoid mistakes, so that foolish critics cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take up your weapons in haste, and approach your patients lightly and firmly, using the best method so that through the grace of God you may arrive at salvation and be praised; and leave behind frightening diseases of serious illness; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish doctor."[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gal%C3%A8ne](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gal%C3%A8ne)
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and cauteries of sharp medicine, and this chapter is arranged from head to toe; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools of cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged from head to toe, with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest lasting in speech and subtle in science and hidden knowledge; and of this, many sages have spoken and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I dread the lengthiness (of it).
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that the cautery is of great help there; while others have said the opposite: that the cautery is not valuable for the illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure a disease caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the opposite, that the cautery brings great help to a hot and dry disease in the human body, speaks falsely.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cool.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And yet, only those who have tested it and are knowledgeable about the chapter of cauteries and the diversity of human complexions, as well as their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and the seasons; we do not fear other complexions, even in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery is among the useful treatments for wounds and of greater goodness than cautery of heated medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not go beyond the member that is being cauterized, and does not harm any other member if it does not touch it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Heated medicines spread from one member to another and bring illnesses with difficult healing to the affected area and may possibly kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this (i.e., spread illness), unless there is an excess (of fire).[Again, please note that I am only translating the text provided to me line by line into English. There may be some context or background information necessary for a complete understanding of the text that is not provided here.]
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experience and from the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me to take away the secrecy which is hidden in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it overcomes the sicknesses of bodies, as the philosophers say in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm that occurs is prevented by the aid of the cautery; and similarly, when the cauterization is necessary and urgent and cannot wait for the time when greater damage does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think otherwise, dear son, as foolish people do; because a disease that is healed by cautery does not return; and they say this; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not only a medicine that changes the complexion, but also dries out the humors that cause pain, and it is worth more than other medicines for its swiftness of action, and for the power and authority of its work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness comes to the patient according to their constitution and the location of the disease and its virtue; and the superfluities are gathered in them through the acquisition of foods and similar things, if cauteries are not administered in places where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries of dens for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the "derriens" (followers) of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cauteries have any value after medical treatment, but their belief is false, and cauteries are the "derriens" (followers) of medicine because when we administer methods of cure in any illness and they do not work, then we administer cautery and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cauteries are the "derriens" (followers) of medicine, not in the way foolish doctors think.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries using instruments of gold are more effective than iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the location of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true as I have experienced, and I have found that it is true in some men; and cauteries of gold are more effective than iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it has cooled down immediately; and if it is heated too much, it burns at the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to toe, so that the vein may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moistening and cooling on the skull, and there are two types of it used for a disease called "soda" (possibly epilepsy), and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for many dreams and toothache, sore throat, and similarly for all illnesses that come from coolness, such as paralysis, numbness, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine dissolving the head (of the abscess) three or four nights, according to what the strength and age and custom of the patient can bear; and then heat up the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something heavy; then place the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and where your middle fingers are, let it bleed a little, then heat up the cautery called "olivare", this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and apply pressure while moving your hand up and down in a circular motion; then quickly remove your hand, and check to see if you see a small hole where the bone is; and if not, repeat the cautery until you do see the bone as I have told you; then take a little bit of salt, put it in warm water with soft cotton inside, and place it on the spot; leave it there for three days; then apply moistened cotton in butter, and leave it on until the heat has subsided; after that, treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacum" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, movement helps in healing.[museum]
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And say some of them that one should let the cautery be applied long enough that part of the bone is burned, and then scrape away what has been burnt from the bone, and have it treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery on for so long and apply it with such force that a piece of bone as large as a spindle whorl that women put in their distaffs is shaved off, so that the humors may be expelled; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one must cure and suture it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every way, except in certain men where there is cause for fear; and it seems to me that I should leave out the second method; for the head is weakened by continuous fluids, as we observe in other members; and even when the patient's head is naturally weak, the first cautery method seems safer and more effective to me, and I use this one to bring about a cure.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	for the old pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes all over the head and lasts long, the patient should use ear irrigation and "cochie" pills, and purges for the head and eyes and plasters; and if they perform the cautery as we have previously said, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly under the cautery that we have mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, perform cautery on each of the horns (cornua) of the head up to the bone, as we have said before; and make a \`leu' (a shallow incision) in the spot called `vasselz'; it is a spot where cups are applied. And keep your hand light so that you do not touch the bone; the patient will feel greater pain in this cautery than in the others, but I will speak of this later. And it is important that the cauterizations on the horns be more delicate than those made on the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery to the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head sudden pain comes, and the sickness extends to the eye, and the cheeks are purged by cleansing medicines, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and all of this helps not at all: then one does cautery in two ways, that is to say with medical liquid and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of medical liquid is: take a piece of elder and remove the bark, then soak it in one or two chiés (a unit of measurement) of medical liquid, and apply the temple where the pain resides, in such a way that you can place the piece of elder under the skin; and when it is placed, bind and hold it tight and leave it for twelve hours; then undo it and remove the piece of elder, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then put on a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, then make this with some burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is in this manner: heat the cautery to a red-hot state, such as this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head has the shape of a clo with one curved pocket, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and place it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn it a little lightly, until half of the thickness of the flesh is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and let there be an abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, put cotton dipped in oil on it, and leave it on for three days; then put wet cotton with butter, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare", at its entire point, and make sure not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of headache.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure headaches as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the previous cautery medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the "cultellare" cautery until it turns white; and thus move it over the painful place in a line half an inch long, and remove your hand once, and hold back so that you do not cover the artery and reach the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when chewing, and the sinew does not look like it is moving and no spasm comes to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear and even for those who do not know about it, and who are not scholars and proven; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop blood flow when an artery is cut, and show you where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not enough for the disease, and the patient is willing, cauterize in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain due to cold dampness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is ear pain due to cold and you have attempted treatments with resolvent medicines and other cures as we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poinse" which has the following shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, prick all around the affected ear, or both if the pain is present in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after making your mark; and make ten pricks around each ear; then cure the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	A torture to be cured by cautery is only one that moves phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this type of torture that moves phlegm from watery eyes and head cleansings and gargling, and if it is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little beyond the temple, and the third on the jawline between the two lips; and place the cautery on the apparent healthy part, and cauterize near the head of the ear a little above and below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a poke; and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the type of cutler's work that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after curing the wound as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and cure it as we have said before.
de litargie	of leprosy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large doses of purgative pills to cleanse the brain; then shave the patient's head and apply on the back of the head the plaster made of mustard seed, as it is written in the treatise on plasters; and that is the method of cauterization: do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If the patient is cured in this way, that is good; and if not, then apply three cauteries on the head, starting from the crown and going down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would any other wound, adding more cautery if necessary, and if the patient can tolerate it, add one in the middle; and if needed, two others on the two temples, treating it until the patient is cured; and use the type of cautery called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the chill or coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of hair and other things that we have previously mentioned; after heating the patient's head, then perform cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, one at the back and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient tolerant, and the illness is strong, then perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be for as long as the most painful spot is burnt, and lift your hand; after that, cure it until it has healed, and use the cautionary device called "olivare" that we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	I would need more context to accurately translate this term as it could have different meanings depending on the context in which it is used. However, based on modern medical terminology, "de l'épilepsie" could be translated to "of epilepsy."
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain of hair and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and tolerant of taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, perform gargling and frequent chewing to cleanse the brain with good foods; after that, heat the head in the middle, and perform one cautery as we have mentioned before, and one on the fontanel and each temple; and if the patient is strong and tolerant, perform cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and weakness of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the method that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is young, perform for him one subtle cautery in the following manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, there are corrupted superfluities or thick phlegm, then use the cautery of mild cauteries, as we have said, for the one who has paralysis.

Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, wrap the patient's head; after that, make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on the head; and have the patient lie crosswise, and be held tightly from all sides; then present the liniment and warm it with old herbal butter; and heat it over moderate fire, so that the wound can tolerate it; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatment, until he is cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or if you wish to cauterize (by making multiple small burns) with the entire cautery, this method of cauterization greatly moistens the brain; and then place a cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyelids
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyelids are affected first by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something that purifies the head and protects against all moisture, and make them sweat or take several baths while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, have the patient bend their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the downward movement of the eyelid condition is present in both eyes or in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are underneath the skin for the entire length of the cauterization, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and be on guard against blood loss, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can with what you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incising, how to stop them with caution; and sometimes fire cautery or hot iron is done underneath the two back bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids from the superfluities, then do the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning as you descend to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the hollows below the two bones; and if more is needed, then cauterize it profusely above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	within the body of tears in the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you have treated the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not improve at all, then give the patient three rooster nights to drink; then raise the head of the bed, and do cautery in the middle of the olive cautery; and do two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery.

Cauteries were used in medieval medicine for various purposes, such as stopping bleeding or treating infections by burning the skin or tissue. Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the papyrus of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery, which is called "olivary," of which the form is as follows:

And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the papyrus is burned, according to the method that I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	on the hair that points to/frames the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and in this case, cauteries are made in two ways: either with fire or with a burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent. Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they (the hairs) grow and are even, then place the patient in a healthy position; afterward, on a piece of paper place a drawing that is similar to the shape of a fern leaf, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered parsley on the eye, then heat up the cautery with the following shape: \*here describes the shape of the cautery\*.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing in the shape that you have marked many times, so that the skin is burned evenly; and the sign of the success of the treatment is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like this for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is healed; after healing with ointment until it is cured.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then begin cauterizing in the same place again, just as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural level, is even, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is what you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a shape out of parchment in the form of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape that you have made like a fern leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in one eye only, then work on it, and if in both as well; and place cotton soaked in egg white under the eye; and let the patient's head be in your healthy position and place your hand over the medicine, and press once and move all the time that the patient feels a biting sensation from the medicine, for they feel a biting sensation like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from the wound.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting (pain) has passed, lift the wound's crust and look to see if the skin underneath is raised as if it had been raised by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is, then it is well. If not, then apply more medicine on the crust where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes (incisions) are well; then put a wet cotton compress soaked in butter on the burnt area until the burn has healed, after which cure the wound from the ointment which is called "dyafenis" and other, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz. If the skin becomes soft and hairs prick the eye, then restart the medicine on the affected area properly, as you did before; after cure it until it is healed; this is the method of the fever leaf.[Note: I'm not sure about "fuelle dou mirte" (fever leaf), it might be a specific plant or herb mentioned in the text that I couldn't identify. Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and accordingly you should adjust your constraints (treatment); and let not the direct path be closed off to one whose goal is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to perform cautery on it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shift; then apply a cotton soaked in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat up the cautery which is shaped like a pen of a writing instrument, bring it close to the head so that it touches the skin; if you wish, sharpen it from one end to the other, and if you wish, shape it like a tent; but in any case, this will be sufficient for your task.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus and the dry matter; and if it is closed, open it up and remove the blockage; then apply hot bran on the cautery, and hold your hand steady with the cautery on the white part above the eye, making sure not to move excessively; and place the cautery in the oil of the eye, causing it to rot.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, that would be good. If not, then perform the cautery again and as many times as necessary, leaving it on for three days; then apply a cotton soaked in butter, and continue the drying ointment treatment until it is healed; but if forty days pass and it has not healed, then use corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and follow the advice of the king as described in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a type of cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and break the skin; then place in the opening a thin piece of material, the shape of which is as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the size of a hazelnut; and hold your hand firmly on the piece of material, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and it is necessary to place cotton soaked in egg white or oil on the patient's eye: the lead will heal the opening of the fistula, and bring about marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer pus to the nose and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose, according to what is necessary in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	from abscesses on the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear on lips that are called "crevices," and the same goes for children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in divisions, and the treatment is unsuccessful, then heat a small scalpel-shaped fire cautery of this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in the cracks until it reaches the base of them; then apply a plug of cerate to the spot until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	for an abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it rots and ruins and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have described in divisions, but it does not improve: then you must use a cautery according to the size of the fistula; place it over the opening/hole of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom of the fistula; do this once or twice after treating the abscess as we have described in cures, until it is healed; and if it heals this way, it is good; but if not, then you must reveal the spot and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but to no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery until it forms a certain shape (as described later) so that you place a peg on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand in such a way that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cauterization as you wish; after that, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and gargle for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the moving tooth is strengthened and the softened gum is constrained, and the moisture (fluid) is corrupted and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether real or imagined, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cautionery in two ways: with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and soak it in boiled butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the power of the butter reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and put it on the painful tooth, and put a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which will follow what comes next, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be relieved on the same day or the following day. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the method of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery to your will on whatever part of the head you wish, and according to what you have power over; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	of scrofula (a disease characterized by swollen lymph nodes in the neck)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulous swellings are of phlegm and of cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-lancet with that which follows the form described hereafter, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side of the lancet not in contact with the abscess; and place the hot lancet on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, then apply a lancet appropriate to its size, and leave it in place for three days; and place wet cotton soaked in butter on top of the burn until the burn has healed; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it has been healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moistures overcome the channels of the pylorus, and also when it is due to a cold complexion, then the patient should be purged first with soluble medicines; after that, cauterization should be performed at the base of the throat, but take care not to come in contact with the throat and burn only slightly. Afterwards, perform another cauterization at the joint between the neck and the spine, using the "clavile" cauter as described earlier; and treat the area as previously mentioned until it has healed.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	about the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. dou cautere de pleuresin	Of pleurisy's cautery.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy from aristolochia roots, in the following manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your finger; and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little further down on the part that is beneath the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining a little backwards; and one cautery in the armpit, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest below the shoulder blade cautery; and do not press your hand tightly, but rather make the movement as if you are smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And some of the ancients said that certain people use a fire cautery in the shape of a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if this is done correctly, the pain will go away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is danger, and either the patient may die or a fistula may develop that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or muscle)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin. Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	Afterwards, put in the two inflamed nerves until the muscle is pierced from the other side, and then pull the cautery out, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves. Afterward, cure when it has become gangrenous for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.
