And if you see harmful humors and the patient suffering, perform cautery on the wrist, and one caution on each side, and two small cauteries next to the large one on the stomach, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Here is a possible translation of the line:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, whether one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupt humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions but without success, then cautery should be applied: three on the spine of the back, which is located directly under the dimple of the sacrum and forms a triangle, and one cautery beneath each buttock.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that the patient's stomach is cold and food does not cook, and the face appears swollen, then apply a large cautery to the stomach as previously described, and another on the liver, and one more on the spleen with all three cauteries being left in place for some time. Afterward, leave the area uncovered until it has healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy part which is called "thigh"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thigh, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it all glowing hot on the cut thigh; leave your hand in this position until the cauter reaches the opening of the vein, causing the blood to flow; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of thigh, cauterize each section as we have said; after that, apply wound treatments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery made of alum, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient is unable to tolerate a surgeon or incision, which we will discuss in its place, such a disease arises that it can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone, and it is inflamed and casts out putrefied matter and corrupt humors, then you should examine it with a thin probe, and make sure that you know the depth of the probe entirely. Afterwards, heat the cautery which resembles a scraper, and insert it into the fistula according to the length that the probe has entered, and continue heating the cautery until the corrupt and putrefied flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, depending on how much is necessary; and beware of burning the nerves which are nearby, and the large veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, then beware of these areas, and do not make an incision outside of the fleshy area, and think that it is not persistent; after healing the area until it is healed, and if the area is raised, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is rotten, and the bone is corrupted at the base; and thus as one of these which we will mention in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Here is a translation of the original Old French text, with added context regarding kidney disease:
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and there is a lot of flatulence and they do not desire intercourse, then you should perform cauterization on the kidneys, one part and the other, with the clavicular cautery that we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and this will bring greater aid.
de la vessie	Here is a translation of the original Old French text, with added context regarding bladder issues:
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform cautery on the outside part above the bladder, where the hair of the groin begins, with one cautery on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the width of a finger; and perform one cautery below the back, or two if necessary; and let the cauteries be shaped as described earlier.
de la marris	I'm not sure what you are asking. The term "de la marris" does not appear in the text provided. Could you please clarify your request or provide more context?
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception to occur, and the menses are corrupted and come late; and when they do come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to perform three cauteries around the belly, as we have said in the section on cautery for the bladder, and two cauteries below the back; and let the cauteries be shaped as we have described earlier.
de la hainche	I'm not sure what you are asking. The term "de la hainche" does not appear in the text provided. Could you please clarify your request or provide more context?
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When humid vapors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip bone with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the separation around the joint as it turns, so that the hip bone is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used for stomaching.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the hip.
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the joint of the hip, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated for what we have said in the division but the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of heavy humors with fetid pills or other good similar ones.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, perform cauterization; and the methods of cauterization are of two types: namely, heated medical irons, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many types, one of which is as follows: cauterize on the boil of the edema three triangular cauteries according to this form, making a good depth and size, and have a space between each cautery the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is done in the middle on top of the swelling, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier for the dislocation of the edema; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire swelling, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used in sciatica, when pain occurs in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and leg, then two cauteries are applied where the patient feels pain, and one cautery above the ankle, four fingers wide, on the left side; and let the cautery be sharp-edged, and let the thickened flesh be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize there where they feel the pain three or four times with a pointed cautery.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, more may be done; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a sharp-edged or circular cautery should be applied, and take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long so as to burn the nerves and major arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and so did the foot, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. After which, they died from a stomach complaint.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, make cautery on one and the other, following this method. // And the wise men say in the cautery for inflammation, of which this is the manner, make a iron such that its head is as big as a walnut of dactyl (a unit of measurement), or just a little less, and let it be interlaced, and let it be so from one interlace to the other at a space equal to the size of a nut of pouch; and let the interlaces be turned on two sides, and let them be like knots, and let there be one well-made iron chain; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heat it until it is completely red and drips sparks, then place it on the boil of the inflamed patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery, and leave it for three days; then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after that, cure it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and I myself have seen few who use it; but nonetheless, this is one of the good cauteries, which can endure it, and where it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from being struck, or from excessive evacuation, or from an expanded cold substance, no form of cautery is effective for these cases, except for that which results from the infusion of a cold substance.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar substances, three lines should be signed on the back, where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line there should be five cauteries or more, according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterizations be done using the type of cautery known as "poins"; and if you wish, perform three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien method, in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have stiffness in their limbs when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the spine of the back, near the base, an appearance which rises above the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it using the cautery of this kind, in this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine evenly. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines away, and let the points be close to one another. Afterward, cure the area until it is healed, as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to a gouty area in a nerve bundle.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain comes from humors that are spread throughout every member of the body, and when it occurs in the feet (which people commonly call "gout"), and when it results from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, it should be treated with cauterization in this manner: make many cautery marks around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to cauterize the sole of the foot, let a single pointed cautery be used. If the pains extend up to the knees and other joints (which happens frequently), make three or four cauteries on each knee, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand away for too long that the thick layer of flesh is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ankles or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and have them take medicines. For if you provide good care for them and purge phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the opening of an abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see that it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that feces descend from their stomach; after, make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has receded, and massage it with your fingers, and apply pressure beneath the abscess up to the bone of the hip, and in such a way that it forms half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [The text here refers to a figure or illustration which would have accompanied the text but is not present in this version. The text continues with instructions on how to use the heated cautery.]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and spurts pus. Then return the bowels to their place; and the caregiver should place their hand so that they do not return; and work well on the legs of the patient, and place a cushion and a servant beneath their thighs, and another on the chest who holds their hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your entire hand, and hold it straight and firmly until you reach the bone; and be careful that the abscess does not burst when you apply the cautery, that you do not burn them, and so that through this the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And the cauteries for children should be fine according to the size of eggs, and also large for large people according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is gone; after curing with other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the boils do not come out when he takes exercise in rooms.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and have him wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not exert himself too much and be wary of excessive consumption of drink and food, and of high laughter; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will speak later about the cure of surgical incision in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of intestinal perforation or rupture
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When perforations appear in other stomachs and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform one cautery with the red-hot iron according to its size, and burn a third of the bowel; after cure as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the iron having three angles in this form: [image of a triangle]
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but sign first the joint's location and make a mark along the width above the break, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire fire-hot iron. But the first cauterization is lighter and swifter.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb, either from falling or injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the "point" cautery, and the cauterization should match the length of the member, its size, weakness, and strength, as well as its location and level of pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that's good; but if not, begin another cauterization on top of it, for sometimes it is necessary for the cautery to move around the limb that is close by, and so you should perform cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from putrefaction of humors and melancholy. When you see a patient to be cauterized, pay attention if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division (of diseases), and does not worsen or persist, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, and another towards the front at the end of the hairline; two more on the temples, and one at the back near the occipital bone; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and just long enough for the scabs to come out, so that the vapors from the bodily fluids can escape; and cauterize according to what is necessary.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and three cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the arms, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are at the back of the heels; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one another on the bone of the stomach, and one another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Know that the more cauterization you do, the more help you give, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person does, because the body is already entirely corrupt. And it is appropriate for the cauteries to be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the forms of irons. Afterwards cure the wound with flour of wheat and honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	The corrected sentence would be: "Après cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis **de enfleure**." (Afterwards, cure the swelling of the wound with flour of wheat and honey and other remedies until it is healed.)
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterization should be done on the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be a little into the flesh of the wound; then cure it with dressings until it is healed. And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed. However, no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of ulcers/sores
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has woken up, and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery somewhat deeply, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and the blood of a swallow and a lark, each of one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and let it air in place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer (chancre) by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer (chancre) appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me at all, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, with a "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot mature or grow. This refers to a condition where a swelling does not develop into a full-blown abscess and cannot be resolved through natural means, requiring medical intervention.
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in dying due to its superfluidity or the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; leave it like this afterwards. For it will hasten in dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery until it is like this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has penetrated the core, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the rotting is eased. Afterwards, cure it until it heals perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	curing with fire through iron (i.e., using a hot iron)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of illness there is, called "corrodens", which is nothing other than an eating away at the member, for it eats the members as fire consumes dry logs. If you see this illness in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauterizing iron, sharp and broad, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and place soft bandages with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption. After this, cure it with ointments generating flesh. And if after three days you see that healthy flesh has not arisen, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on those parts of the corrupted place that remain. And this eating away has sometimes been cured by medication instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for the medication in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of athlete's foot that comes to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	It often happens that on the feet, due to neglect, an illness arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large, swollen thing that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this illness is of two kinds: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is as follows: heat up one iron rod as thick as a pen of a goose quill, and made of good metal, so that it can pierce the corn from all sides, and have sharp edges; then place it very hot on the corn, and turn your hand all around the corn until you reach its base; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster of crushed marsh mallows with oil, and leave it on all night, and the corn will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with an ointment promoting flesh growth until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they (the corns) are turned inward towards the body, and this happens often on hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this way: take a cane of iron or copper, or a goose quill pen, and place the corn and warts on it (the cane); put it over it so that it surrounds completely, then add some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the corn, and let it find a deep path for the hot water to reach the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will detach completely from its roots. Do this one after another, until you reach all that are on the body, then cure them with ointments promoting flesh growth.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of trembling/shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If someone trembles from coldness of nerves or quartan fever or otherwise, then you should make 4 cauteries or 4 of them on the spine at the base of the neck, one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the hip, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	"foul-smelling pustules" or "putrid pustules"
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	"Sometimes, from behind, one sees the body covered in foul-smelling pustules that come from large corrupted matter. In this case, it is necessary, as soon as they appear, to apply the cautery to each pustule: a subtle probe made of myrtle wood, whose tip has been heated in the fire, or with a root of aristolochia longa, or with a lenticular cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, using this method, and they cannot grow any further, but rather the excess matter from which they come is broken up and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood."
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often, there is a large flow of blood from the cut artery to the wound, or to the incision of an abscess, or to the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger and no more comes out; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both small and large, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.[translated by Taylor R.](<https://community.duolingo.com/comment/43267959$comment_given_id=100%3Apost%3Fid%3D43267959>)
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts to bleed again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, quickly take another one from those in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and make sure no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped easily, especially if the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have mentioned: with a cauter, by extracting it when it has not been treated, by tightly binding it with a bandage, or by using medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will treat tight restraint with tightly wrapped cloth or by placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone who does not have any medical supplies with them, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and apply firm pressure until it is stopped above the wound and the vein; and they must not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood coagulates, thickens, and stops flowing; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases that require fire cautery or heated medical instruments, and we have discussed their causes, tools, and forms; and I have arranged this chapter from head to foot, and in this chapter, I will follow the same path so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is appropriate, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to undertake folly. For many types of people come to be cured, some of whom are so afflicted by their illness that they easily die due to the violence they find in their disease and the severity of its malice; and one should fear these.[*]
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And there are some who give you their trust and say: "Wait, I am healed." The illness is contemptuous. It is not at all appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you in this manner; instead, put more effort into your honor than into your greed, and open wisely for those whom you are certain of, and from whom you can gain both reputation and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that their health may be restored; and this will help you to acquire good renown, and glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may the Lord give you understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have divided this chapter into sections for you, as it is before the chapter on cauteries that I have explained to you from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a full or swollen head (lit. head full of water)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often occurs in children during childbirth, and it happens when the birth canal applies too much force to the child's head; and sometimes it is caused by unknown reasons.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and in all that I have seen, death hastened; and for this reason, it seems better to me to abandon the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the skull thickened each day so much that it could not support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone at the siphac, between the brain and the bone; and the operation is such if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the head a wide opening; and let it be as long as .ii. fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the mouth open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not respond, then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all pus; Afterward, compress the wounds with cloth and powders, and put wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then unbind it, and care for the wound with bandages and ointments, and also keep the head binding; and give dry food to the patient in small amounts of liquid until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the swelling of the abscess is prominent and where the collection of water is; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, incise there where the abscess is prominent and the collection of water is, and shape the wound according to your ability; and make sure that you do not cut the artery; and if a flow of blood comes, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of pus.

Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In which case, for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; and when they are loosened, cure with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery as long as you work on it, then quickly cover it with cautery or fill the wound with vitriol and press on it firmly until the bleeding stops; and if you do not have this on hand, place your finger over the wound until the blood clots, and keep pouring cold water over it until the bleeding stops, pressing as needed; and a more gentle and easier method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with this two-sided cutting cautery, but make sure that the edges are thick to maintain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and when you have marked the two places, place the heated iron upon them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be far apart because this fire cautery is not solid all throughout; and that is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears flowing from the eyes come from the veins that are above the temple of the head and medical treatment does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsation on the forehead like a tremor; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the paper has been heated up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called it "cure contuse", and it consists of shaving the patient who has this disease's hair on their forehead, then making three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, extending down to the eyebrows, and the other two should be at the temples above the eyelids, taking care not to cut the arteries that are located at the temples above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the jawline, and each wound should be three fingers wide at its widest point.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and plenty of rags to wipe the blood, then apply the following styptic: (two parts of)

dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting a catarrh frequently, and you see the eyes sunken and small, with weakened vision and inflamed eyelids; and the hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that those matters and those catarrhs do not come out of one vein alone, and the proper cure for this is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And the treatment is that you tell the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another of about one inch. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, cutting down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves near the temples that move during eating. Once the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then insert cotton between the two lips of the incision and apply bandages. Then bind moistened cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, being careful to avoid hot abscesses. Once they have been removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way, take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; then apply it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or creatures, or mineral stones such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something falls into the ear, such as a stone or any other thing that does not attach itself to the ear or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, put a few drops of violet oil or sage oil, then facilitate extraction; and make him sneeze using condiments, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards. This cure often works; and if it does not work, facilitate extraction using fine pincers, of which this is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a fine hook of thin wire; and if it does not come out that way, then make a probe of tin and insert the head of the probe into the hole of the ear forcefully, and stop what is around the probe with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the probe; then pull it out strongly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take birdlime, which is used to catch birds, and place some on an instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all of these things that we have mentioned, then hurry to pierce the ear so that abscess and scab forms; and the manner of this piercing is that you first make an incision on the patient's head and draw blood according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area or where it hangs; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, coming to the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck on it with your mouth; and continue this treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is infected and swells, perform an extraction; and if it cannot come out, apply a thin spatula in this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision on the grain. But do not do so when you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing of condiments first and fill the ear with soft cotton. And lie on the same ear where the water is. If it comes out by itself, it's good. If not, take many small and light pebbles, heat them slightly by fire, and put one or two of them in the patient's ear, and jump on one foot from the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and it will come out completely; and if you want, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the thickest part of the reed is burnt; then do the same thing again with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said in the case of stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then perform extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help at all, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then pull them out with fine forceps, and if you don't see any, then take a probe of the kind described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow below and wide above. Insert the thinnest end of the probe into the ear according to the severity of the patient's discomfort, then push the entire probe in; repeat this frequently until all the worms come out. If they do not obey and come out, then stop up the probe with cotton as I have said in "la piere"; and if they still do not come out as we have said, then administer the distillations that the ancients have proven to work in the treatment of worms, which can be found in the treatment of distillations; and then drip your oils and medicines into the ear using this entire instrument, as you see here:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation; and have a well-made brass instrument to press the distillation in, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you choose of your medicines into the probe, and keep the probe in the ear; then insert the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a small pot heated by fire so that it can be distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The blockage of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Any child is born who has no hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from wound or pus inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small pock near the hole, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that goes deep and cannot be seen is of difficult healing in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, it is necessary to expose the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage clearly, work on it with this instrument, which is its shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and blunt at the front and back, so that it does not injure the ear; if the blockage is from pus or flesh in the ear, hold it with delicate tweezers and gently scrape it out until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the blockage is deep in the ear, take a delicate lancet, heat it slightly by the fire, and place it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the blockage, make a small incision gently, taking care not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert a wick into the ear according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder made of crushed vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then you should remove that tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made from roset oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, then soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
