de la gresle	The term "de la grésle" is a medieval term that can refer to hail or a type of disease. Without more context, it's difficult to provide an accurate translation. However, in the following phrases, "grésle" may be translated as "hail":
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times on the eyelids come things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this illness is called "grandine"; it is a collection of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: take care if the grandine moves from one side to another, and this is easy to determine; then make an incision of appropriate size, then gently scrape each part, then use tweezers to remove it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the skin a little, do not worry about it; and if the wound is large, attach it with a suture and cure it until it heals; and if it is small, do nothing, for ointments quickly restore it and cause new flesh to grow.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine descends inside the ear toward the upper part, turn the paper and extend the grandine with tweezers, and remove it while pressing from one side and the other; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, this does not matter; and when the grandine has been removed, irrigate the eye with salty water and cure the wound until it heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is instilled on paper sheets, and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they have a discharge at mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie down on their faces and sleep, and their papers beneath their eyelashes are moist, which causes swelling and covers the appearance of the exinach that is apparent in the eye. And when you press the area around their eyes with your hands, you can feel the exinach coming out between your fingers.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of this procedure is as follows: the patient places their head on your lap, and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach present in each part, then place it on top; and press with your hands from both sides so that the exinach comes together in the center; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a sharp scalpel-like instrument, and let it not be any larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the leather until you reach the exinach; and in multiple ways, the exinach comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it all in one piece with the cloth between your fingers outwardly, and turn your hand to left and right until it is dispersed; and make sure not to press on the incision, so that you do not reach the whole scalpel until you touch the eye and wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit wound does not appear at the beginning of the incision, slightly increase the incision length until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then wet bandages in oil and water, and place them on the wound, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that has remained, then cure it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the place, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	I believe there might be a word missing from this text. Here is my translation:

There are four ways to treat this: through cauterization with fire, or through medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and suture or by blisters, depending on what I will say.

And it sometimes happens that the hairs of the paper are converted (i.e., become entangled or stuck together); in this case, you should follow what we have said about making an incision; but stitching in one and the other is more difficult (i.e., requires more skill).
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of gangrene is as follows: and it consists of folding the paper and making an incision according to what I have said, and then making two incisions with skill, and two thin threads as long as the paper and as wide as the space between the eyes; and bend the two corners of two parts where you hold the threads; then bring the two thin threads together gently on top of the part of the paper above the eye, and pull the two threads firmly from both sides; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin that has been pulled will die and turn black and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, strike it again with force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is knitted together, and the skin is raised, and the hairs will no longer poke out; and this is the shape of the two sutures that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.

The procedure is as follows: take a fine needle and thread a soft, fine silk thread through it; then bring the edges of the wound together and tie the thread gently, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then place another fine thread of silk next to it and tie the ends of the threads; then put the patient's head in your lap; and do this in a sunny place so that the procedure is well-lit, for it is a delicate and small task; then insert the needle through the entire length of the needle into the root of the hair adjacent to the wound, and quickly push it through the skin until it comes out above the natural eyebrow hairs; then pull out the hairs up to the tip of the needle and insert the pulled-out hairs into the needle, whether there is one or two or three or more hairs; then remove your hand so that all the hairs come out through the entire length of the needle along with the natural eyebrow hairs.

And if the suture is removed and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the suture downwards below the thread that you have placed until the suture comes out of the opening above and you can see it with your eye; then pull both the suture and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days until the hairs become embedded in their place and new growth appears; and if the hairs are small, then attach one long hair from the natural eyebrows and lift it up with that or let it hang loose until it is lengthened, then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of eye putrefaction
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or gangrene comes to the eye, it happens in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly due to wounds, cuts, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	The method of treatment for this in the eye is to split open the abscess, separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside until it heals; and it should not be treated with drying or constricting substances during the cure. For if you do so, the disease will return worse than before. Instead, use softening substances such as fenugreek; and let rosewater or aloe and linseed be cooked, and ointments of diacatholicon melted in some oil, and wrap it with a bandage to cure it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	The key to your treatment is to ensure that the abscess does not close in its previous form; and the procedures we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness that is underneath, truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and split and cautery and similar things; and the method of the work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it in the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and bind it with one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the appearance of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits on the side within the paper; and let the ends of the two splits be at the two corners of the incision that you have made, and make them into a corner so that when they are assembled, the appearance is like the appearance of a letter called "griesche"; then remove the flesh according to the width of its sides that extend below the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with the medicines we have mentioned, softening agents, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you must make an incision in the paper at the site of the hairs, as described above; and then separate between the two sides of a bandage as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters should prepare with all their power how to make the appearance return to its natural form; and the patient himself, depending on what is required for the work and instruments in several dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to some men in such a way that the paper above is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should insert the point of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you reach the thin membrane (subtle spatulum), which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient can endure the sharpness of the spatulum and not damage the eye; and make your incision, by which you flay the joined area, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and cleanse the entire joined area, and at times use salty water, and sweet and clear collyrium (eye medicine); then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and put wet wool on the eye with an abundance of egg; and after three days use the collyrium and other wound healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid or corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the eyelid is of two kinds: one is fleshy and similar to a hard zit, and another one which is not fleshy but looks like frozen white mucus, which when touched with an iron tool and attempted to be grasped with forceps, cannot be; and both appearances begin near the outer corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient should place his head in your lap, then open their eyes. You lift the eyelid with your hand and pull it taut with small forceps, then stretch it out; then take a needle, and put a horsehair or cowhair, or beef thread in it, and bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the eyelid, and perforate through to the other side. Then bind the eyelid with a strong thread, and stretch it out, and flay the skin of the eyelid that follows the lashes and hair follicles up to the eyebrow; then cut away the remaining part at the root of the corner of the eye with the subtle scalpel and small forceps, leaving the natural flesh or corner of the eye intact so that the normal flow of tears is not interrupted. Sometimes the eyelid heals on its own with a thread as we have said. Then it is flayed with the whole soft spatula, which has the following shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the retractor does not touch the fleshy towel and break it, and that the iris is not pierced; and after the incision, put a little bit of crushed oil into the eye, and of a collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this type of insensitive nail is often cured with medicines; and it grows as I have mentioned in the division; and if you see it covered, perform the eye operation on the patient, and take the retractor that is slightly sharpened according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully pare down the nail above, and if you see that it does not become thinner and the edges come together, distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red collirium and crushed oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then begin the other task according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, such as an abscess, then leave it alone; first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin around the eyelid hinders the eye with great harm, suspend it at the eyelash, and cut out a part of it and not all of it, so that tears can still reach there; then distill red bile into the eye which is made from lithargyre.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Here is the translation of the given sentence:
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Here is the translation of the given sentence:
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Here is the translation of the given sentence:
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Nevertheless, it is necessary that you lighten the cure for each weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in ironwork; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that these members can endure the work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that are located over the eye and hinder the vision's function and weaken the eye all days. Therefore, it is necessary first to check if the eye, in which the veins are present, is healthy and has no other illness but sebel; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently suspend those veins with your fingers according to your skill, and make sure that the fingers are gently pressed in this way:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two fingers arranged gradually in one row in this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then when you have carefully constricted those veins, and wiped away the blood hour after hour, until you see the swollen veins recede from the eye; and take care not to poke the eye with the ends of the cauterizing tools, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not injure the veins; and once you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to break down any remaining pus.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to do all of this in that hour, make a poultice for the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and you are certain there is no danger of abscess; then resume according to the previously described method until it has healed; this is the method of constricting:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The masters call this type of fistula "arissati"; when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have previously mentioned, but it is not healed, there is a trick to it: you must make an incision on the abscess, at the point where it should burst, and drain all the pus that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, take all the instruments which are in the form described here; and it is called "rough head", and make it of iron one cubit long, and point it like a file as in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place the "rough head" on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press down firmly until you feel that the corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicaments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is healed and flesh has grown, and the skin of the wound is healed and remains so for forty days without any inflammation or other adverse event, then know that it is healed; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the bone as follows: reveal the bone a second time with iron, and with moist medicaments, and when it is revealed, take a three-pronged iron pin according to this form, and the head of the pin should be made of iron with three angles, and the shaft should be tapered towards the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the pin next to the bone near the lacrimal duct, and move your hand away from the eye about an inch, then turn the whole pin until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of breath if they keep their hand on their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicaments as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows back and the wound heals, the matter will go to the nose; this is an easier process for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket/orbit dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide all around and there is no trouble or reduction in vision, then bind the patient; next cauterize, then apply leeches or cups without striking to draw blood, then place a mixture of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocollex on the eyelid; then bandage the eye and cover it with bandages and soft cloths; take care to use enough soft cloths, doubled in four layers, and apply them gradually according to how much is needed for the eye; next bandage firmly with a hard bandage, and reapply the cups without striking to draw blood; then remove the cups and leave the eye bandaged day and night, and if the mixture softens, tighten the bandage again; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see that the eye is healing, it is good; if not, reapply the mixture, bandages, and leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of retinal detachment
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a disruption in the retina, it becomes visible and appears as if there are grains of resin on the paper; this is frightening to see. If you view such a detachment, the procedure is to insert a needle into the root of the lower part all the way up to the upper part, then insert another needle with double thread in the corner of the eyelid. Pierce it and leave the first needle as it was placed; next cut off the end of the doubled thread and use it to tie around the edge of the retina, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a soft, wet cloth soaked in egg on the eye. Leave it until the threads stick to the retina, then treat the eye with comforting remedies until the wound heals. Sometimes, the wound is restrained by a circle of cloth around the edge of the eye until it has healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from within the eye, and let the watery humor run out, and let the eye descend and go in again; then pull it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the swelling of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a swelling that forms in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of appearance of this illness is such that you should have the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then hold their head with both hands and move it until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then let it be punctured and let the light not descend and fall, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatula and insert it through the transparent cornea, along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the corona, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or boiled water with fenugreek and honey, into the eye, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similarities of waters in the division, and that which it is necessary to pierce; and one must work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind his good eye very tightly; then place the paper on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the size of a grain in that bend of the eye at the side of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" valiantly, and turn your hand until it pierces in the bend of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the grain to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; and you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horned tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it under one way after another. If the water comes down now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the water rises in the second duct, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and it no longer rises, then gently remove almagda by turning your hand slightly; and then put in a little bit of gem elixir and raise the eye inside. Then place cotton or wet wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white on top of the eye, and bind it with the good eye. We, and those who are of our time, place a bread poultice with plenty of egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", whose shape is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And perforate the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle hole, then place almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping aid, in which he may sleep on his back in a dark room; and be free from all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to left or right, and bind him according to his condition until three days have passed; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then replace the binding for seven days; and it is necessary that you do not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but rather lighten this, so that the water may rise quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	if pustules occur, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards the one who soothes swellings; and when it has calmed down, then loosen the vision and place a bandage on its edge for a few days, and let him always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house rarely and briefly, and turn your attention to your duties; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almagda perciet, which one can suck the water (juice) from, but nonetheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor do I read of it in books of ancient knowledge; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see (them); and they should be made of pure tin:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the tops of them be of this same delicacy, and the rear parts in three sharp points.[translating "agues" as "sharp points"]
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes different kinds of flesh are born near the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such where the flesh is swollen and of a foxy color, and others that have soft flesh of good color. In this case of these flesh growths that are soft, but not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply the instrument to those flesh growths, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp, thin spatula on one side, until you know that the flesh has been completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with all one instrument very delicately and lightly, so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as appropriate; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood stops and all the flesh growths are removed, then pour vinegar or sterilized water into the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose does not open and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that flesh has grown in the bone above, which the instrument cannot reach. In this case, you should insert a fairly thick linen thread, with small knots at regular intervals (about the width of a fingernail or less), and place the patient's head with the thread in its nostril to the best of their ability, and pull gently while sniffing until the thread comes out of the nose into the mouth. Many children do this in school, and it is an easy task for those who wish to do it. Then hold the part of the nose that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel your way along the knots until you know that they have become embedded in the flesh. When you are sure that the knots have lodged in the flesh, pull out the thread gently, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment before reinserting it into the nose as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment dissolves all remaining flesh. Then insert a piece of plastic tubing into the nose for several days until it heals, and use drying medicines if necessary. This is the method of using the instrument to purge the head, which is used to distill oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, such as a candle, and the wick similarly; and if you wish, make a closed candle, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often arises in the head of the nose a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it all, then place the cautery or hot medicine on the wound; and if you delay cutting it until it has grown, see if it is hard, of purple color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an abscess that has festered, because when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of purple color, and you see that you can cut all of it, empty the patient and cut the wound without fear, and cure it with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been cut and sewn[References:
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must scarify all the edges of their wound until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a suture and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood and ground incense on it, and place on top of the powders a piece of strong plaster or another binding plaster, and leave it until it comes off by itself, then cure it with an ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men, hard abscesses like grains of pepper appear within the lips, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply a poultice of powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stopped; and then apply goose grease, and cure the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a hardened flesh is born on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of abscesses or inflammations. The term "sordes" in medieval medical texts often refers to purulent, infected matter or discharges that accumulate in the body and need to be drained or cleaned out. So "des sordens" could refer to the treatment or removal of such abscesses or inflamed areas.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, hard and rough crusts form on the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, or green, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you must make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape off any visible tartar, crusts, or stains from the teeth until nothing remains; and do the same for black, green, yellow, and other stains until they are cleaned; and if all of the buildup is removed during the first cleaning, that is good; if not, resume cleaning on the second and third days until everything is removed; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments to clean them, depending on what the task requires, because scrapers used to clean between teeth have different forms than those used to clean the surfaces of teeth; and make sure you have these shapes and others prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because one should not do this hastily; for it is a very serious matter up to the point where there is no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is constrained to have it pulled, you must make sure of the tooth that is causing pain. Often times, the pain leaves the patient and they think it's gone, but it persists despite pulling the good tooth; this we have often seen done by quack dentists. And when you are certain of the tooth causing pain, you must sear around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum all around; then pull it with your hands or fine pliers at first tug and tug until it is well loosened, then securely fasten the pliers; and have the patient's head in your lap and hold it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and carefully pull it with pliers so that it does not break while pulling, and you must work very delicately around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take good care not to break it and leave a part in the patient's jaw, which will cause greater pains than the first due to the malice of the root. And be careful not to act like ignorant dentists who sometimes out of haste and recklessness break the tooth socket and do not treat it as we have mentioned; instead they bring about great illness because of the roots that remain or because of the broken tooth, which we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, rinse the socket with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the socket with powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should be long and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick shanks so that they do not bend when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and serrated to hold teeth in place.
de la racine des dens	on the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains to be pulled, then you should place cotton soaked in butter on the spot for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then use tongs called "algefri," which have a shape like a bird's beak; and they should be made with a lime-like texture, and this is their shape:[ST1] It is not clear what is meant by "and c’est li forme" in the original text. I translated it as "and this is their shape," but it could also mean "and that is the shape" or something similar.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all of these tongs, then you must cut open the flesh all around the root and place in it the instrument called "althali," that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:[ST1] It is not clear what is meant by "c’est a savoir palainche" in the original text. I translated it as "that is, a scalpel," but it could also mean "namely, a scalpel" or something similar.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots come out through this, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which forms are described later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one can help themselves with this instrument that has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front of the teeth's root, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments that are not mentioned here; and the wise master subtly finds his own instrument, according to what his work and the disease show him, because there are such diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity; and one does not break the cart or other bones, where it will rot, but instead searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and able to hold the bone so that it does not splinter, but can instead hold and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, then use all of this instrument for it.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is crooked compared to the other tooth, take this tool, the shape of which is shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hold the instrument close and keep it in your hands for several days due to the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file like the one shown here in form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is similar to the file used to make needles; and carefully and lightly file down the tooth, holding it still until it is loose; then use a plane at the end for smoothing, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the filament and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers and align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, and position them so as not to injure the tongue; and then leave them tightly in place as long as they can endure, and if they loosen or the wire breaks, then constrict it with another wire; if they remain and function in this way for their entire duration, this is the method for realigning two healthy teeth and two loose teeth, as you can see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place, as we have said, as fresh as possible; and let no one who is not wise and skilled interfere; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the empty socket and constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is a ligament under the tongue that is natural at birth or occurs accidentally due to a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and hold their head, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its anchorage. And if there is hardness or a knot due to the healing of a wound, insert the hook and cut the ligament widely; and make sure not to cut too deep, as the artery is beneath it. When you have finished, apply a little rose-colored or cold water, then place a linen bandage underneath the tongue. Have the patient hold this in their mouth every night so that the ligament does not heal again. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder to it; and if the wound becomes infected, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then continue treating it until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then place the "oncine" (a medical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, then apply vinegar powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift it up with ease and support, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come within the throat growths that are called "godath," and they are properly called the "two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, beware: if it is an abscess of hard consistency and bluish color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it at all with iron, so as not to cause bleeding; but leave it until it has ripened, and then you will open it, or it will break open by itself; and if it is of white color and swollen, and the root is thin, then have your instrument ready to cover (it), but first look to see if the hard swelling is at rest and calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and open his mouth and take it with his hands, and press down the tongue beneath the entire instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine brass as a scalpel:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you press the tongue down with all this instrument and see the abscess, then take the "oncine" (a medical instrument) and insert it into the almond (growth), and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, which has the form of forceps; and yet the cheeks are curved inward towards each other and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool at hand, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have bent one of the almond-shaped parts, bend the other in the same manner; and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water and vinegar; and if there is an evacuation of blood, gargle the patient with water or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it has healed; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almond-shaped parts, so cut them in the same way as the two almond-shaped parts.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess in her throat, which was quite large and had closed up her entire throat, such that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained like that for one or two days. The abscess was so large that it had pushed out two veins through the two nostrils. I acted quickly and inserted a probe into one of the nostrils, then pulled it out and extracted a large quantity of pus; I did the same thing in the other nostril, opened her mouth and pressed on her tongue; then I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut into one part, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew larger again and filled up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; then I applied pressure and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left from there, not knowing what God did with her after I left.
de l’uve	of the eye (uvea)
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».
