Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is fine, then it is necessary to make an incision; and the one that is rounded assembled and not long; and it is sanguine or of a fleshy color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision in it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye and pull it down, and cut along one of the two edges that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut further than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a trick with cauterization without fear. And the method of cautery is sharp and pointed. And it is that the patient places their head on your shoulder, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and apply live coals, so that they are not too thick nor too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have the patient have a hair on their head, or place the medicine in it, such as the teeth of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause harm; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for the duration of half an hour, until you see it absorbed and the irritation of the medicine has calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument full of cotton into the wound above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery of the medicine, then do so, and after the cautery, clean around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elderberry and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in one pot, and place a spout on it; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And whether it is of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes should be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the temple, until the eye becomes mortified; then reapply it frequently, until the eye dries out, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it at all except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to overwhelm the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat, it is then necessary to remove what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what does not appear to you and is embedded in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit after food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of thread, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will become stiff, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take an instrument made of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and hold the head high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, nor force the bone in; and it is better if the patient inserts the instrument themselves, so that they know where the object is; they insert it downwards, or pull it out with the entire instrument evenly, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinus
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the vein is treated, as I have said in the division, by medical cure; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after pressing their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the vein, then pull it with a tiny hook, or with delicate tweezers worth for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a bladder leaf, and put it in the sick person's throat, then put a hot iron on the tip of the bladder. And do this often. And if the patient becomes thirsty all day, then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a pierced cloth, and in this hole put the opening of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the bladder in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the vein; and the vein will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the vein, when it can be seen, is similar to curved pliers so as to easily enter the throat; and it should resemble the beak of a bird of prey, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what the following remembrance brings in this book, one after the other, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own likeness, and those that retain moisture. And the second manner is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different than those of the base, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different than those that come in joints, and each one must be judged in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is completely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the base, so one must pierce it when it is dead; and one should not pierce an abscess that has grown without digestion completed, except for those that are near the base, lest it rots inside and becomes elongated, forming a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of piercing the abscess when it is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the cessation of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the lowest part of the abscess, where it is most prominent; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and on all sides where there is no curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And in those that are curved, according to the curvature of the member. And when an abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better to leave the incision until it has solidified after digestion is completed, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body's fluid will be elongated and full of filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, depending on the need of the member. And in small abscesses, make small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core and cover it. When it has become as one cloth, and has died, then do the same as with tumors: and there are some that are split into three angles, and there are some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses of the glands; and there are some where a round incision is made, and other shapes and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no visible abscesses, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce them; and it is necessary, when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, not to draw out all the pus in that hour, but only some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and then draw out some more; do this many times, gradually, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak vitality, such as women, young children, old decrepit men. For the spirit sometimes jumps when the pus is coming out, causing the patient to suddenly die, and you would not realize it. Therefore, be very cautious in this matter and, once you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a flat cut, then apply tension bands of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses with many holes, then it is necessary to place a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of the skin in the abscess and turned it over, then it is necessary to fill it with old linen rags or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and a damp cloth to the area multiple times. If the bleeding persists, provide care and treatment, using the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, then place tents and damp cloths soaked in wine and warm oil on top; and if it is summer and the area is fleshy, then apply damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, for three days as we have said; and then loosen the abscess and clean and dress it as needed until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.

Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where small abscesses of the head come, and they are of a type that are in veins, as the joint of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty and such where there is moisture, like pustules; and some are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. And the work of cutting consists of testing with every single instrument called an "entromissoire", of which the form comes after, what thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, one should pierce it from above the long [part]. And when the moisture has been emptied, one should skin without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again if anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain from the night will clean it. And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are certain that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound with a suitable ointment, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds a hard knot, one should cut it lengthwise; and insert your fingers, and skin it all around, and put all your effort into removing the cotte where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I told you after. And similarly do for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And some of these abscesses, either on the head or where there is no moisture, are not like others, as was one of the abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess just like a hard, rough and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had struck it, they would have made a wound just like from a stone. In other abscesses coming on the head, except those that come on children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the incision should always be at the lowest point, so that pus may easily exit; and cure them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	"Scrofula" is a medical term used to describe a group of diseases characterized by the presence of swollen lymph nodes, typically in the neck. The term comes from the Latin word "scrofa," which means "she-pig," likely because the affected lymph nodes can resemble the swollen glands of a pig. Scrofula is also known as "the king's evil" because it was once believed that the touch of a king or queen could cure the disease. This belief dates back to the time of King Edward the Confessor in England and was continued by subsequent monarchs. However, this practice has been abandoned and there is no scientific evidence to support the idea that royal touch can cure scrofula. Scrofula is usually treated with antibiotics, but surgical removal of the affected lymph nodes may be necessary in some cases.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	"Scrofula" often occurs in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes appear in other parts of the body, and are connected to each other. Each scrofula is specifically located in its own node, like the knots and abscesses on the head, as we have said; and there are many different kinds of scrofula. Some contain moisture, while others are malignant and do not want to submit to treatment. In this case, if you see a scrofula with good disposition and similar in color to the skin, and it is not swollen in the nerves of the neck or arteries or ducts, and is not deep, then you should cut it open from above, and skin around it on all sides, and pull out the two lips of the wound as needed with your fingers, just as we have said for abscesses of the head; and remove little by little, making sure not to cut nerves or veins, and that the scalpel is neither too sharp nor cutting, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop blood and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skilled judgment if there remain any small scrofulous patches, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous patch, it is not appropriate to cut that scrofulous patch at its root, but bind it with a double strong thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut all of the scrofulous patch, it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it now, so that there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofulous patch. It is necessary to focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said. Those scrofulous patches that have an accumulation, pierce them where it is clear; and pierce it as was said before, depending (on the location), then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a running ointment, until the flesh is healed.

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the operation (or cutting) of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglotte" be cleared; and this is not done with help, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are blocked by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two amygdales.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to incise the epiglotte, it is necessary that we make the incision under three or four circles, a small slit crosswise, between the two circles or according to the size of the syphac, not in the cartilage.[Leading modern medical sources state that an incision may be made in the epiglottis (also known as "laryngotomy") to secure the airway during certain surgical procedures.](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK534796/)
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those places are suitable for the incision of the epiglotte where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and narrow.

Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that this should not be done until the throat is completely stuffed up and the patient is judged to be at death's door with respiratory distress.

I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that it had not received any venesection or surgical attention except for the throat, and the wind was escaping through the wound.

de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "goiter hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a jet, and it is very common in women;

Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of dislocation, that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissors," according to the form which will appear in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inspecting the abscesses of the nose is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, as much as you know the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the probe, and take care that nothing extraneous comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs corrupted (with pus), note its color, as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the probe there is no moisture, know that it is fatty, then make an incision in the shape of a cross and take hold of it with forceps, and gently scrape from each side and around where it lies until you extract it cleanly with the pus.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot extract it whole, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.[ST1] Here comes the next sentence to translate:
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pain will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if some of it remains, and the wound troubles you, apply corrosive powders to the wound and bind it, place a warm and soothing poultice on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the pain is great, cut the two edges of the wound, and treat it with remedies that clean out dead flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the boiling blood is against you or something else, hasten and use the liquid of broken vitriol, and let it stay for two or three days until the wound putrefies and the ebullition of the blood settles; then apply a new covering to what remains.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of the intrusive instruments, which are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses or fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	"And they are similar to the needles used to sew up surgical wounds, and they are made of yellow brass, iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and they are tested by being dipped in black pitch to encircle the abscess fistula."
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	"And they come in three types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings."
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	"The shapes of the needles are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are some needles that have two bowls in three types as well."
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	"And there are some needles that have three bowls, and they too come in three types; and there are needles with two bowls only, and those with one bowl only, and all of these are necessary in their place."[Note: The word "corbeures" is translated here as "bowls" but it can also be translated as "scoops".]
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	"The tips of these needles that are used for sewing are sharp, and some only cut on one side, which is used to scrape the flesh so as not to cut the vein or nerve."[Note: The word "nous" can be translated as "flesh", "meat", or "tissue". I chose "flesh" here.]
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these instruments, the needles are attached to handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And they come in three types: large, small, and medium, as you see;

et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must act according to the form of this line b through g.

et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the breasts sag downward and are weakened by their size, similar to what happens in women, then make two incisions on top of them in a similar manner
