et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient will not rest, or due to blood loss, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive substance;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it dissolves the remaining flesh and fat, then continue to treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulous swellings or they have cores, and some of them contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Then those that contain moisture should be lanced in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply a suitable ointment to it until it heals.[*](footnote: The word "ceu" is not a standard English word. It might be a typo or an Old French term that was not properly translated here. I translated it as "it" in this context, assuming it refers to the wound.)
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulas, lance it as we have said for scrofulas, and if the wound becomes pus-filled again, apply a hot iron as we have mentioned before.[*](footnote: The word "devant" in Old French means "before," referring to an earlier part of the text.)
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin above it sticks together, it often results in abscesses, and the same happens when the vein swells and becomes abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is recognized as being due to an artery, the abscess will be long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your hands, if it is due to a vein, you will feel a pulsating sensation, and when it is due to the swelling of the vein, it will be round and bulging.[incision](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/incision) sus aposteme
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is located under the armpits, groin, neck, and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Then one should avoid the cure of iron, and also avoid touching the one who is at the head, and in one who is swollen from an artery make an incision above the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then perform the incision as in operations past, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then place a needle beneath it and make it pass through to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;[2](https://www.pitt.edu/~dash/surgicalinstrumentglossary.html#needle)
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then pierce the place between the two ligatures with an intromittoir until the blood within comes out, and let the abscess be released;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then provide the care needed for healing, and allow the ligatures to fall off as they become loose;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with a suitable ointment until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then you should apply your hand to the abscess and press it firmly against the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the area that you are holding with your hand, and guide it through so that there is a double thread, which you can pull from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess as I have told you, with one of the two ends of the double thread at each of the two ends of the incision;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you are concerned that the thread may come out, then insert another needle at one end of the thread under the entire length of the abscess to the incision made by the first needle, and secure the thread in four places;[Instructions for using a fire cautery, dealing with blood loss and treating an abscess]
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then lance the abscess so that the excess comes out, then lance the excess of the pus and leave what is attached;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then provide treatments of bandages and poultices until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can occur in the artery and vein, an abscess can also happen in the nerves when they are wounded or from excessive labor and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this occurs more often in the shoulders and arms, and in all places where there are joints, and these are painful abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the skin, and they are in various dispositions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is strongly constricted, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the chest;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it moves well in all directions, and does not go either forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: for there may be contracting.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is on the head or forehead, makes the skin suppurate.[References](http://www.gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/btv1b9069573n/f23.image)
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then suspend it with a string, and peel it, then remove it and stitch the wound closed, and care for it until it heals.[References](http://www.gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/btv1b9069573n/f23.image)
des grosses boces pendans	of large, dangling breaks/fractures
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there occur in the belly and not elsewhere what is called "funge," which resembles them, and its roots are thin, and its excrement is large; and there are small ones and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two in his belly that resembled "funge" more than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were open, and moisture flowed from them continuously.[Notes: The word "fungi" is used as a general term for various kinds of growths in the text, but it's not certain what exactly they are referring to. It could be fungal infections or something else that resembles fungi. Without modern medical knowledge and tools, it would have been difficult to accurately diagnose such conditions in the medieval period.]
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces; and the appearance in the incision is such that you can see if the patient is moist, and the color of the flesh is white and moist and of fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	and if you cut it with a broad spatula, and have the cautery prepared in your presence. For when cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overpowers you, then hasten to use the cautery;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, take a well-made flax thread, and tie the sinew as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	Then hold it taut and do not stop holding the flax thread taut until you cut through the sinew and feel no resistance; and if the roots are thick, there is a risk of cutting through the belly as well, but you can still safely cut only half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Afterwards, cauterize it so that it does not grow back; then treat the wound and make sure not to cut the tendon which is of a fleshy color and has poor sensation and looks like an eyelet.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts open.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery of a wound or a crack in a syfic, and is above the belly and in the groin area, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries, according to what is before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to the rupture of the syfic and the opening of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it protrudes and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing, and it is clearly apparent when pressed with the hand, and does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, it is easy to touch, and the procedure is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you should leave the treatment. Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or a swelling, then you should instruct the patient to expose their throat and lie completely flat, then bind tightly all around the swelling;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	and then command them to lie still between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	and then go around the place you have marked for the entire duration,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch out half of the abscess above with a large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk tightly, and make sure the knot is secure.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open up half of the abscess which is stretched out on the thread and insert your index finger, and search for the intestines.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught in the thread, then untie it, and put the intestines back into the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find a swelling (or pustule), grasp it with the hook and cut away the excess;[INST*](Note: I assume "boueil" means "swelling" or "pustule" in this context)
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein resists you, then go around it smoothly, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have created in a cross that you made to pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then constrict the abscess in four places around the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave it in place until it dries up, and let the pus drain out by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or cut it when it has become thin and dried up, then treat what needs to be treated, and shave the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as needed, and close the wound.[ST1]
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the chancre swells in the groin, and requires great caution in its treatment. And the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, or on the thigh, and similar places, one must completely remove it when it first appears. And when it becomes large and old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never cured any; nor has anyone ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make them sweat if they have obvious bloating; then prepare the patient for the procedure with one good location for performing the operation; then cast your leeches or chancre and all the hairs from around it, and remove everything without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe clean the area with your hand or some other object, and if the bleeding caused by the incision of the artery or vein is contrary to you, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then cure the wound with another cure until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only in this case; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hydrops archis, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the patient is weak, or if he has some other illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this way:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Leave the patient upright in your hands, and have the assistant press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula according to this form: And make it sharpened on both sides, but yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot cut;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must cut three fingers' width above the navel straight down along the groin; and if it is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the navel three fingers' width; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it should not be that the patient lies on the incision so that the excess does not run to this weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce through the skin with the instrument, and push it, and lift up all of the spatulum between the skin and the syringe as when flaying to the quantity of a fingernail or thereabouts; then pierce the syringe until the spatula comes to the visible opening, and that is the water's place, then pull it out and insert this instrument of which this is the shape: And it is similar to a thin silver gutter, and is made of light iron or copper, and has in its lower part a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other, and one on the other; and the incision is cut like a pen nib, and this is the shape of the incision that the writers cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	on top of it is the collector, so that when the instrument reaches the water, lower your hand now onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is appropriate at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit from the weapon, or they will fall unconscious, or they will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the quantity of their strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength indicate, and their pulse; then pull out the instrument and hold onto the water, which is now held back by the cork that stops the hole above the syringe, which I mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then reinsert the instrument the next day if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw off a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this for several days, and be careful not to draw off too much until only a little water remains. And if you are in doubt about the patient, and leave too much water, then cure them with burial or hot sand, and let them sweat a lot or bathe in the sun, and let them drink; and cure them with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes a child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place. Then it is necessary that he wait until he is four years old before being pierced with a very thin spatula of this shape: then insert a fine plug of linen into the opening and bind and hold it in place for three or four days; when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him do so, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out may not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	The one whose opening is small, it is treated with a plug of linen as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are wounded, because some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the glans, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient lies down on his back, then stretches out the head of the penis and holds it in the shape of a pen's nib, so that the opening is in the middle as it should be; and be careful of bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with a styptic and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean all of them, then put a cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with Diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of pus-like appearance and discharge, then you must apply cautery to it. After cutting it out, and if the ulcer is in the middle of the penis, with some of it under the skin and some outside, you must remove the part that is under the skin first; and when it has healed, then cure the outside part. For if you cure it while it is still attached, there is no certainty that the head of the penis will not be pierced, leading to blackening and corruption on the penis and in the urethra; so you must cut out all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from honey, flour, and the outer shells of pomegranates, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, you must apply the lunar cautery in this manner: The cautery is helpful for two conditions together: namely, bloodletting and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert a piece of willow cane into the urethra so that the patient may urinate through it. And when the skin on the head of the penis has been cleaned (this occurs in those who have not been circumcised, as well as in cases of wounds or abscesses), you must then scarify it with a thin instrument until the ligaments are loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a serious matter to discuss, you should scar it with a small spatula, either at the tip of the foreskin of the penis or the skin; then carefully separate it between two layers, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water, but not wet again.
de la circoncision	Here is the revised translation with "de la circoncision" added:
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as the loosening of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this work willingly and particularly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest one for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not use circumcision for their children since it was not part of their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that most masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one thumb's width and with force, using a novacule, avoided the area because there are two layers there, and perhaps they cut the one above and leave the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they cover it up, and the pain is doubled, and with the cleansing of the wound from the thumb's width, there is no certainty in the cleaning of the wound; and during the cleansing of the nail, perhaps the iron slips and ruins the work, and many times it happens that they do not need to clean it and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the cleansing performed with force along the entire length of the incision, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces (surgical knives) cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, you cut evenly in one steady motion; but the thread should be tightly wound around the skin; and the way of the first work is that you make the child think that you are only tying the thread around the shaft, and then you make him happy in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then place it in your hands straight, and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the infant does not see it, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the spine and blow or cough, and pull upwards until the head of the spine is in; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then bind the area with a double thread, then bind it to another ligament; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then quickly lift the cough above and pull the head of the spine.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the abscess drain, for this is beneficial; and put powder on it and on the powder a cloth glued with a half of an egg cooked and tempered with pink water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two heads should be sharp and even, and should be of equal size to the little finger.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleaning is when the core within runs out at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail so that the place forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is beneath the groin is swollen, leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and gently flay it; cut as you can move it, and be careful near the part of the groin, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound of things that have grown together with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut beyond measure with a knife and it goes too high, it will not harm; heal it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of urinary retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Urinary retention is caused by blockage due to a stone, coagulated blood, pus, flesh grown inward, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that its retention is due to a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over their knees; and have their feet placed on their back, and stretch their belly over the dorsal part, and tightly constrict the patient's abdomen as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the expulsion of the stone above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of thin and light silver, like bird feathers; and its cane should be a palm and a half long, and be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the way to release urine is that you take a double thread and tie a bag of wool or cotton at its end, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and push it up to the tip of the syringe. Then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and pour oil (moistened) and olive oil and warm water over the bladder and the penis;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the base of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly. Then push the syringe forward to reach the bladder, and let the patient feel as the urine flows into the empty part, and this is not done in any other order except because the conduit through which it passes is twisted. Then pull the thread gently so that all the wool bag follows, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it outside and let the urine flow.[Source](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seringue_%28m%C3%A9dicale%29#/media/Fichier:Syringe_medicale_du_XIIIe_si%C3%A8cle.jpg)
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and refill the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and straighten out the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or if pus has accumulated, and you wish to distill water and medicine into it, then use an instrument called a "clepsydra," which is shaped as follows:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see. The hairs on the opening through which the medicine flows should be such that they effectively block the urethra without requiring additional support, allowing for the removal of moisture when necessary and insertion when needed.[STHAP] Et li verges de ceste clepsedre est faite en tel maniere qu’ele puet entrer et issir par l’un des .ii. pertus d’une part, et que li leus chevez soit couvert a celui d’autre part ou il n’a point de pertuis;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you wish to insert your medicine into the bladder, place the end of the funnel in the moisture and pull on the drawstring that is attached. By doing so, the moisture will be drawn up into the funnel, and then quickly push the drawstring back in to prevent any from spilling out. The moisture will enter and reach the bladder, which the patient will feel.[STHAP] Et quant tu veulz que li medicine soient entres en la vessie, et puissent faire leur vertu, si tiens le chief de la clepsedre par dessoubz les testicules du malaide; et puis trais la moistor dedenz par l’un des .ii. pertus d’une part, et boute le rod ens par coi li medicine court; et quant ele est toute entree, tu remetras l’autre rod a son lieu, qui est sans pertuis, et serras bien les vaisseaus por que la moistor ne puisse issir.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	"and this is the form of the subtle enema with which to irrigate the bladder: it is as follows:"
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	"It is made of silver or brass, and the opening is high up; and below it has a loop where the ligament hangs. Then take a sheep's bladder and put the liquid you wish to use for the enema in it, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a strong double thread, and heat one end of the liquid over the fire. Then insert the tip of the enema into the urethra, then squeeze your hand over the bladder until all the liquid has entered, so that the patient feels that the liquid has reached the bladder."
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	"And if you don't have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make it into a circle, and pierce it all the way around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then gather the circle as one would gather a sack, and put inside what you want of oil and liquid and water, and tie it to the instrument. And do as you did with the bladder, squeezing your hand until the liquid reaches the bladder."
de la piere	"from the stone" (in this context, likely referring to a kidney or bladder stone that is being treated with the enema)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with their medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone stuck in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates with difficulty, and urinates frequently, and then becomes rigid; and there are many of these jumps; and the foundation is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when it comes to the treatment, first, it is necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the filth that is in the intestines. For it often interferes with finding the stone.[br] (Note: The word "clistere" refers to an enema.)
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then, lift the patient by the feet and straighten them out, moving them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and protrudes somewhat outside; then make the patient sit between your hands, ready, and let their hands be under their thighs, so that the bladder is completely lowered; then search for it and touch it inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	if you feel the stone in the area, hurry to cut into the stone. And if it does not fall at the first touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is elderly, or your middle finger if the patient is a mature adult; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it towards the bladder neck; then press upon it with your finger, and remove it to the side where you intend to make the incision.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to lift the hips with his right hand and remove the skin beneath the hips on the side where the incision is made; then insert the spatula, which has the following shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make the incision between the area of the hips and the perineum, not in the middle but near the left testicle; and let it be directly above the stone, and your hands should be placed firmly on the perineum, and let the width of the incision be greater at the outside than the inside, and adjusted according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Perhaps the pressure of the hands on the perineum will cause the stone to come out easily without effort; and be aware that some stones have angles and sharp edges, making them difficult to extract; while others are softer, similar to a gland, and round, which makes it easy to extract.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To the one with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not break open, you should pull on pincers that are like a file at the tip, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you place under it a thin curved instrument at the tip; and if you can't trick it in this way, widen the opening a little more, and if the flesh closes up again, constrict it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are multiple stones, place the largest one at the neck of the bladder first, then cut on top and extract it, and then the smaller ones if there are more. And if they are very large, they must be smoothed out, and a larger incision must be made. For two things can happen to the patient: either they die or urine constantly comes out through the opening that the flesh cannot close; but still try to extract it, or break it apart with pincers, as much as you can remove it in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, on top to calm the hot abscess; then raise the patient up by their neck and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the area well with oil and water, then clean it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses or ulcers come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained, which is known to happen without pain with urination: then put your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound of water, pus, and decay, and help it in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that during all the times that you care for it, you bind its two thighs together and apply the medicines to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra and lodged in there, and urine cannot exit: then care for it as I have said before, cut it many times, it is excused from cutting for this treatment. I have proven this myself.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron fork of this shape and make it with three sharp points on one handle.
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take a thread and tie it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, as much as you can, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will flow, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod. It will break immediately and exit along with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because of some hindrance, then tie a thread beneath the stone and another above it; then make an incision in the rod towards the stone between the two ties, then remove it and untie the tie, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the female stone (i.e., a calculus or concretion in the female urinary tract)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it does happen, the cure is difficult and hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled midwife who can examine her, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this hand art; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than the stone of the man, for which reason a deeper cut is required, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, you must summon help, then you must take a very skilled midwife, but they are hard to find, and if you cannot find one, then at least find a careful and clever male physician; and present them with a bowl of water, or a woman who knows about the art, and command her to do what you command her regarding the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it downwards under her finger, and command her to insert her hand into the vagina of the sick woman, and search and press firmly with her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then she should move it gradually from the opening of the bladder to the root of the thigh; then place yourself on the stone at the root of the thigh towards the middle of the vagina, where it is most prominent and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and the first incision should be small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then put the knife in the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound so that the stone can exit, and know that there are many types of stones: that is to say, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and with corners. So know their appearances to recognize the evacuation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood overcomes you, put vitriol powder in its place, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the necessary instruments ready that I mentioned in the extraction of the stone for men to assist you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overcomes you, and it is an artery that is cut, put the powder on the wound and bind it with bandages and do not unbind it again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, because the patient may die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wound dries, then return to your work, until the stone is out.[1](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caut%C3%A8re)
de hernie carnouse	of a carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the groin, and contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin between the white humor that we mentioned earlier; and this only happens in cases of hernia.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramice is due to weakness in the groin area, and this matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it can result from a blow to the groin, and this moisture can have many different colors: it can be yellowish in color, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and there are other possibilities as well.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this abscess, for if it is white pus as we have said, the abscess is ripe, that is, a long swelling like an egg's shape, and the corners do not appear, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper membrane, the abscess is ripe with a part of the egg, and therefore one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the corners and the white membrane, it can be felt well; then when you want to know the color of the moisture, squeeze with an instrument that is a quarter in size, which forms what is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the insertion, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their ability and the fullness of their body; then have them lie on their back, on something a bit elevated, and place many rags underneath them;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then have them lie on their left side, and command the assistant to sit at their right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the loins;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the scalpel and cut through the skin of the loins along its length down to the pubic bone, and make your incision straight dividing the skin of the loins until the white abdomen, and carefully remove the skin according to your ability;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the bladder fully with water through one large hole, and extract all the water, and then put your fingers in, and stretch the bladder upwards; and only touch the kidneys but not otherwise; carefully cut the entire side of it in pieces so that if you do not cut it well, the water will come back.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg (bladder) jumps out of place during your work, then replace it in its proper position once you have completed the bladder operation; then sew together the two leaves of the kidneys with one stitch, then cure it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg (i.e., the abscess) corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie up the vessels that are supportive, while being cautious about the flow of blood; then cut along the entire suspensory vessel and remove the egg (i.e., the abscess), and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if water has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two branches (of the vein); then cut the other part in the same way as you did the first, then wipe away the blood and put a woolen cloth soaked in rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put thereafter another woolen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and place the two pieces (of flesh) on top, and place folded bandages on top of that, and bind it all up with a bandage in the shape of this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two bandages and stuff them with threadbare wool in this shape and sew them at the collar of the breeches, and let one of the pieces go under the buttocks up to the back, and the other on the side where the (patient's) hand is; and let the other two pieces be on the two corners, and let all be tightly bound together with a belt around the waist of the breeches.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes, this branch of cautery is medicinal in place of an iron cut, and it is that you take one scalpel-like cautery, and cut the skin of the buttocks, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing water is revealed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Take the cautery in this form, and pierce that pus-filled boil with it, and peel off the skin with this sharp, heated cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut it in all ways that you can, as much as you reach all around; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg (?), and know that this work is more healthy; and pay attention to prevent bleeding, and be careful in the procedure of cutting.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if any thing opposes you, whether it be a bad abscess or bleeding or anything else, then cure what is opposing you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this procedure due to its horror, perform perforation as I told you, that is, when you are completely certain based on the signs we have mentioned that moistened ramie is present.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part, making the incision the width of a finger's breadth, and place the perforation through to the depth of the body; and let the opening be wide enough that all the water drains out.
