Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic conditions occur when the opening of the female is not fully developed or is small; this can be natural at birth, or caused by an illness or disease; it can also be caused by a growth, a subtle or thick syphilis that develops in the womb, on the sides, or beneath, and prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes even menstruation. The recognition of this condition is made through observation of the vagina. If the obstruction is visible, then you can use your fingers or a probe. If the syphilis is subtle and close to two pounds in weight, hurry and proceed as follows: place your index fingers together, have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two pounds firmly until the subtle syphilis protrudes and covers the obstruction; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the area; have the woman lie with a man every day, so that it does not heal. If the syphilis is hard and thick, you must cut it out in the shape of a myrtle leaf. If the obstruction is made of flesh, then lift it with tweezers and remove it; use hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and egg yolk; place a wide plastic tube so that the wound does not heal; proceed in this manner for a long time, and apply a linen tent to keep it dry; then cure other wounds until it is healed. And when flesh grows in the womb, you must remove it in this way, if it is not enlarged abscesses. For an enlarged abscess in the womb, do not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	Des hemorroides (of hemorrhoids)
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into piles; and we have previously mentioned their likenesses, and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment. I say that both hemorrhoids and piles, when they are inside the anus, and they are not noticeable to touch, then they are not cured by cutting. Those that are at the opening of the anus, which one can feel, are those that can be cured. Therefore, it is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the piles with pincers and cut them at their roots, then apply dry medicines that constrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet on the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes out, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and thicken it with honey and egg whites, and make a plaster on her back. And if it stops, it is good. If not, then apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without piercing; then take wool, and soak it in willow juice or oak gall with old wine, and heat it up at the place. And when the abscess subsides, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, and it should be covered as I have said for piles; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that can appear in the anus, such as chancre and abscess pious, herpes, eczemas, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and other diseases which I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary in this treatise to discuss the hot abscess that appears in the anus, which is not one of those that are incised with a lancet; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look and see if the abscess is hard at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if it can be seen. Then do not rush to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats for him to recline on, and support his back and elevate his legs above the thighs; and spread his thighs, and place his arms beneath his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then turn him towards his right side, and prepare the instrument used to open the anus, of which I will give you the form later; and it is necessary when you are preparing this instrument that you insert the rod first in order to know the depth of the anus, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the anus with cloths so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary for him to place the funnel of the instrument above, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens and is pierced by hand gently, then it should be covered at the tip, with a small spatula; and once the pus has drained, then put in the wound moist compresses of rose oil or dry green oil; and place the compress beyond the wound deep inside the anus, and place above the anus and below the tail clean wool soaked in water or malvasia cooked; then cure it after two days with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and sometimes lift the anus and wound with an enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and aristolochia longa cooked; then return to the ointment. And if the wound is closed in the anus, then be careful not to cauterize with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural form of childbirth and its signs, which are as follows: when you see a woman pushing downwards and craving strong smells, then know that this birth is in accordance with the natural form, and the baby's position is under its head and the afterbirth is with it. And when you see these signs, then gently press on her stomach so that the baby comes out quickly, for as soon as it rests on its head, the afterbirth comes out with it and the woman is cleansed of her excess by good purification. But if it comes any other way, then it does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes with its feet first, or outside the body, or the hands, or it comes up to the stomach, or turns around to the neck, and in other bad positions. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in these matters, and be on guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how one should help in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out head first in the natural position and the woman is having a difficult time giving birth and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be held by other women. Then anoint her womb with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked and place the small spatula (whose shape is described later) between your fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split open the afterbirth, cutting it to the length of your fingernail where the moisture is, and press on the woman's stomach until the baby comes down. And if it does not come down, then give her an enema of musk mixed with fenugreek oil, then have her drink something that will make her sneeze and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour, and the baby will come out now. And if both hands come out first, then gently press them back in one by one, and if they cannot enter, then have the woman sit on a stool with her feet raised high, and slowly lower the stool to the ground, making sure she does not fall. If both hands still cannot enter and the baby is dead, then cut the hands off with the knife that has been placed here and extract the baby, and press back in this way as well.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the child's coming out on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When a baby comes out on its feet, you should lift it up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it gently back and forth until it is evenly aligned.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take one of its feet and stretch it out, moving it gently back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If it can jump up to its hips, instruct it to catch it, and make it sneeze with medicine;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps willingly, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, turn it a little and a little, until it is according to the natural shape.[Reference(s):
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not move as we have said, take a small amount of althea root, oil of cumin, and melted gum, and grind all into a powder in a mortar;[Reference(s):
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and apply a poultice inside the woman's nature and on top of this;
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in lukewarm water up to her chest;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and once she is wet below, make her wear a necklace of myrrh and put it on her, leaving it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat and make her sneeze, while pinching her mouth and nose, gently pressing her belly, for the child is coming now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	at the birth of the child, onto her knees[...]
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, place the doctor's hands all over and over.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then let him be propped up on his neck, and let his legs hang down, and let him lie on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands over and over, and then take hold of its hands on the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is fully prepared below.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not cry, take hold of its feet and move them vigorously, then move its belly upward, and place your hands there.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and turn the child over and over, and tell the woman to push until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's birth which comes out holding a hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to manipulate (it) to bring the hand back:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if you cannot bring it back, have the woman get up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, make her lie down on a bed, and spread her legs widely apart;[ST1]: [original: s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;]
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then apply the manipulation that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she doesn't give birth, make her sit on a seat, then study how to reset the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And deliver the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and tell her to pull until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the child's exit on its neck, and have its hands spread open, and its face turned toward its mother's back.

de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four at once; this is not a strange thing, and it rarely happens.

et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And do in this way as it is worth for their health (or: as it matters for their salvation).
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes children are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise and glorious [one].
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary for the physician to know all this, because by chance similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	and he should act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child[or "of a stillborn child"](Note: this phrase is taken from the previous context, not directly translated from the sentence provided)
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a stillborn child or a closed womb, as I have mentioned in the section before, and it does not come out, and you are required to perform manual treatment;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	then you need to determine if the woman is of good health and without any complications or fear of death;

et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the attendant should place two pieces of wood (or something similar) on either side, securing her to the bed so that she is not moved during childbirth;

si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	then you should take a pointed spatula between your fingers and make an incision in the head to release the fluid.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can use the instrument called "almidach" to make an incision, using the tools or chapter that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And do the same if the child has a large head naturally.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pull out the bones with tongs,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the hips jump out and are held in place with a forceps, then they should be split open, so that the moisture which is in the abscess can escape.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if it cannot come out, then cut it to pieces with a knife as finely as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the delivery will be easy and it will be easy for the child to be directed towards the mouth of the womb.[STT\_3]: The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or the breast, you should pull it out using a cloth wrapped around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and open up the belly or the breast, until the moisture that is inside comes out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	And if other members are amputated and the anus remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	If the surgeon puts his hand deep into the wound, and pulls it out to the opening of the wound;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then put in one thin probe or two, and pull it out;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the opening of the sore is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, it should not be worked on;
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	instead, moist and greasy things should be applied;[Ori 3:57 PM]
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply plasters, and soak it in warm, softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is lying on its side, and you can make it even, then do what we have said for the live child;[Ori 4:01 PM]  [Continued in next message]
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if there is no power to set it [the dislocation], pull it out by pieces, and leave nothing of the sinew. (referring to the tendon or ligament that may be hindering the resetting of the joint)
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if it improves as we have said in regards to abscesses that come from the disease;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with a tight bandage and other remedies should be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a fetus had died and then another was sewn onto it, but the other one also died.[Source: Medieval French medical text from around the 12th-13th centuries.]
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed an abscess in her buttocks, which grew so large that it burst open, causing severe infection.[Source: Medieval French medical text from around the 12th-13th centuries.]
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, and was unable to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster, and there came out a bone, and after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly at this, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	And so I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I examined the wound and pulled out several bones until the woman was in a better state;[INTUITION]
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And the woman lived for a long time in this way, and frequently urinated a little at a time.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I have only included this chapter because when the master finds a foreign object, he should know how to apply treatment.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the dislocated part to its proper place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the press, which one should use to press books; and it has two turners for the two cheeks of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, let the corners be thinner than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth of the funnel be 2 fingers wide, and the edge of the branches 1 finger, and one and a half palm long;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And between the two limbs there should be two joints of this same funnel, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or slightly more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two joints are inserted into the mouth of the funnel to open when turning the two horns.[1](footnote: The text uses "marris", which is a variant of "marcisses" or "marices", a term used for a surgical instrument with two curved parts, like forceps or tweezers. Here it seems to refer to the funnel-shaped instrument mentioned earlier.)
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made from ebony or boxwood, similar to the shape of tongs or pliers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And let it have two joints at the two ends, as you can see, one palm long and two fingers wide;[1](footnote: It is unclear from the text whether these dimensions refer to each of the joints or to the overall size of the instrument.)
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you wish to open the wound with all the instruments, have the woman sit on a bed, her legs spread apart and hanging down.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then place the two attached forceps into the wound, and hold the end of the instrument beneath her thighs.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with all the instruments, just as you did with the forceps, according to the size that you wish to make the opening of the wound, so that it becomes however wide you want it to be.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all sharp and have many similar versions; and when the surgeons have prepared them, their work is quicker and higher for the people because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not to be excused.[Note: This sentence suggests that it is important to make sure that all necessary instruments are prepared before starting a surgical procedure, and that one should not look down on any particular instrument as unimportant or unnecessary. The word "despire" can mean to disdain or reject something as being beneath one's notice or unworthy of consideration.]
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the cervix is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with medicine, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she gives birth by this means, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If she does not give birth by this means, she should take a pot and make a hole in the cover, and put inside herbs that can open the womb, such as chamomile, rue, aniseed, camomile, casia, and centaury.[
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	Cook all these herbs, or some of them, in a pot of water over the fire; then place a reed or the hole of the pot at the mouth of the womb,[
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And let them steep until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the sinews pull quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, order the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of sediment or marsh mallow juice, and then insert it into the nature (vagina).
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And look for the sinew; and when she has found it, so take hold of it and pull it out gently and directly, so that the patient does not feel pain during the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but she must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and become detached.[Notes:
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the wound is too narrow, we have said that the treatment is to induce sneezing and perform fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	"and if it doesn't leave any of what we have said, make sure not to rush in pulling (on it)."
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	"but it is necessary that the one who is at the opening of the wound, you tie him to the thigh of the woman, and then give him an enema of tetrapharmacum ointment."
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	"it will purge and heal her, and she will recover; but nonetheless, when it purges, it can cause a bad smell in the stomach and head, and wound the patient."
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Then it is necessary to use appropriate fumigations for that person: some of the ancients have proven the effectiveness of fumigation using watercress and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained menses and afterbirth is as follows:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it looks similar to a dog's paw, and one places the delicate head into the natural position, and the legs wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be above the coals, and the blister until it is burnt, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but instead it is stopped up with a delicate styptic.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, it is necessary for the wet nurse to pierce that styptic with her thumb, and not with a sharp instrument, and make sure that she does not touch the wound.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply the ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will swell, place a piece of wood into the wound, and leave it in for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these stoppages come from a sudden wound or abscess; in this case, the wound must be covered and treated as we have said with a piece of wood.[Reference(s):
de la fistule dou fondement	of an anal fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Anal fistulas are swollen lumps that form under the anus and grow to the outside of the body or within a two-finger space.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is a fistula or several; and when this lump is old, it works, and furthermore moisture softens white pus or thin pus,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is a discharge or swelling when the patient passes stool, and perhaps also in urination.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the groin.[`screen`]
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And so one recognizes a persistent fistula in the anus, and not persistent.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and this is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and then carefully inserting a thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula where there is no curvature.[`screen`][Instinctualization: None]
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is curvature, insert a slender stake of wood, or a horse's hair, until you feel the stake or the hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and no purging or wind escape occurs from the opening, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it has not penetrated; therefore, hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or the conduit of urine, if the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has penetrated to the hip joint, then the probe comes to the site itself.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the origin of the pain around it, then it is already bent, and neither medicine nor heating through ointment helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure except for surgery, and it is mere labor and foolishness of those who meddle with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In one that is neither Persian nor old, there is hope of cure by iron, as I have tested.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and the patient lies in your hands on their back, and raises their legs up to their thighs, with their thighs inclined towards their stomach.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then insert a tent of iron or wood if there is twisting, until you know where the tent comes out.[ADD: It seems that "tente" here refers to a probe or a medical instrument inserted into the body to diagnose an issue. The sentence could be translated as "then insert a probe of iron or wood until you find out where it ends up"]
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the bottom (of the back), you should insert your index finger there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if then you feel that the tendon has been pierced; and if it is exposed where you feel, between your finger, the groin or the flesh, then know that it has been transfixed.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	do not trouble yourself to try to heal it, as it cannot be cured.[Reference(s):
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is true, however, that one can sometimes cure such cases, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the help that is provided consists of heating the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put it all hot in the fistula, until it reaches the bottom; and do this twice or thrice, until you are sure that the decayed cartilages, which look like a bird's feather, are burned.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then cure it with wet bandages smeared with butter, until the decayed flesh comes out, then cure it with a wound dressing that draws out and heals the flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, that is good. If not, there is no other way to heal it;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if the bandage enters and does not reach as far as the finger at the bottom, and there is a thick covering of flesh or abscess between your finger and the bandage, then you will see the fistula following the thick covering of the wound.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC...]
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the fever begins at the onset of the fistula, and you push the bandage further forward, and then apply the cautery afterward until it reaches the end of the bandage.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	And the abscess will be drained and will fall; then clean away the decayed flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and nothing of it should remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flow is too strong and cuts between you and the procedure, cauterize it with fire or medicinal powder.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of the decayed flesh and the drying up of blood and the removal of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then, in order to treat wet abscesses, use butter or crushed herbs until the area becomes numb and the decayed flesh falls out into the pus.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with hard, dry plasters, which are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is healed, it is cleaned and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is separated from the body, then insert your finger into it and examine (the condition).
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the hardened part (tumor), and between two (fingers) there is tissue or a syphilitic chancre or flesh, or it is near to breaking through, then there should be no hesitation or lack of confidence in applying one of the following three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the base, or if possible, insert dressings and treat it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too deep, so that you do not cover the support that holds the foundation, and allow the evacuations to come out through it willingly.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it has been cut near the foundation, using a tent or another pointed instrument.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the cavity in the wound as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then try to restore the wound and keep the fistula on the outside of the foundation; this will be an easier task for the patient.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are of this kind: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is next to the base by the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	Take a probe pierced at the end in this way:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted wire through it, and insert the probe entirely along the wire into the fistula until it reaches the base.[4](#footnote_4_0)
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is perforated in the margin next to the base, then draw out the wire from that hole, just as you insert your finger into the base.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	And pull out the head of the wire and bring the two sides together, pressing one against the other, and leave it like that for one or two days;[6](#footnote_6_0)
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and he restrains some times, as long as the son binds those things that are between two, and tightens.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cures the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not at all appropriate to cover the incision when it is so deep and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spathulate needle with which one makes a fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	And on the other hand, no, so as not to cut what should not be cut, as you see here:

Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids come in two forms: they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed.

dou fremit	in a trembling state.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica (ant) is a small, hollow defect in the body, going very deep into it.

de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema syringe
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is an enema made with silver or brass, or melted iron or lead; and never are these instruments small or large, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are prepared for use in children's care and those who are weak and suffering are small (in size).

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously spoken in the division about wound treatment; now we will tell you of hand and medical treatments, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or a spear or stick or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or wounds are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs.[IST] Ou selonc la matiere de quoi il est faites; si com plaie de feu ou de poison.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for reminders will come in their own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, pay attention if it is from striking by a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And if you suspect a hot abscess: then cause it to drain immediately from the head itself if blood is oozing from the wound, and let the discharge be on the side opposite the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And avoid giving the patient rich food and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine, on the wound if abscesses are prone to form;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh and still bleeding, and not yet exposed to air, a powder which I will mention shortly.[Note: The "poc ci aprés" implies that the author will describe this powder later in the text. Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure. et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and roasted barley, as well as poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotting flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the decayed flesh and discard it, then cure the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or a vein that cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, bind it with a thread.

And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: and that is to apply this powder which solidifies once the wound has moved (i.e., been cleaned).
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, three parts quicklime, and finely grind (the ingredients) into a powder.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly until it dries out completely and becomes one with all its blood.[Original text implies that the application of the powder will dry the wound out and help in joining the skin together.]
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And then bind it well and leave it alone without loosening, if there is no swelling; for the medicine should not be removed until it has healed.[In this context, "madicine" refers to the powder and any dressings used to hold it in place.]
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Sometimes, quicklime is used alone if incense and dragon's blood are not available, but only after the wound has been cleaned by the practitioner.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has moved (shifted) itself, it should be left as is, and this powder should not be applied at all.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey, until it (the wound) dries up.

de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, except if a nerve or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound open and not apply any restricting substance, for that would harm the nerves and cause them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member.[ISTOP] et se tu veus qu’il soie bons sanz grant dolor, si doit on la chaleur du membre recreistre;
