And if it cannot be healed, and an abscess forms, then know that there is a fistula; cure it as is appropriate.[(](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/fistule) A fistula is an abnormal connection between an internal organ and the body surface or between two organs.)
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it is simple, whether on the belly or the back, then cure the part in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large and requires stitches, then sew it up. If it is small, use powder. And if it is close to the bone, and there are fragments in it, then clean the wound and remove any loose pieces;[notices that "la plaie" is both singular and plural in this sentence: "clean the wound(s)" will work]
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not separated, let the wound rot, it will lighten the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and the judgment for other wounds on other limbs is the same as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"the rupture of the stomach" or "stomach rupture" would be a possible translation for "dou derrompement dou ventre". It seems to refer to an injury or trauma to the stomach that results in it being torn or ruptured.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the stomach can be large, medium, or small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Sometimes, with a large wound, the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, which can cause their introduction (or insertion).[START OF ORIGINAL MESSAGE] Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et quant il advenist que les ners de l'intestin sont hors du ventre, si est ce perilleus et esteit puis ferez qu'il soit remis en son leu. Mais se tu ne peuz faire autre chose, si taillies les nerfs qui sorent hors du ventre, pour ce que li intestins n'i soient empechent, mais il est perilleus. Li autres membres sont souvent ataint et blessez par la grant plaie.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	therefore one inserts intestines back in with heat, if they are not put back in place with heat;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, making it more difficult to insert them back in place.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And therefore, it is better to stitch up the median wound, because one can more easily return the intestines to their place in that case than in the other two cases.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that there are four types of ruptures in the abdomen:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common sutures happen on the stomach wound,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And yet, they are more suitable with the stomach suture, and I will name each one and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestines protrudes,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	And a hard thing it is to reset [a dislocation], this can be done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or through the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is frozen, warm it in the following way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you cook in vinegar, cypress, and spikehellebore,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and insert the intestines until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes use this constrictive wine, which is often effective in reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling recede, rinse the intestines with water or with ale and malt cooked together.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for this makes the opening less tight and allows for easier passage.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot be entered, make an incision at the wound with the instrument used to cut piles;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	And the first remedy is to cut (what is) bleeding.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that no one should cut into it without great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And the instrument for cutting is...[INTERRUPTED]
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	...to cut inside the curve and not outside; and here is its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines come out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	place them back in their natural shape in their proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	If you have the power, for it is worth more to act.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and located in the lower abdomen area,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so you should make the patient lie on their back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the area below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then place the head and chest higher than the parts below (the affected area),
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	And similarly, if there is a rupture in one of the two sides of the belly,[INSTI: si doit il avoir le chief plus haut que les pieds d’environ .iii. pies;
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and pay attention that the injured part is placed higher than the others;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus one should manage as I say for both large and minor wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use what is at hand,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have a compassionate servant who can touch the entire wound with their hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring the edges together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of suturing,[INTO](The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or needles, according to the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave one digit space from the edge of the wound and insert a needle with a strong, good thread in it;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pass through the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the incision,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	(which is underneath the skin inside), until you make it pass through from that side,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the two edges of the incision in four places;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then tighten a doubled thread around the needle in two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then bring the two edges of the wound together,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave a finger's width of space and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread to it just like you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and continue doing this as many times as you need, depending on how many needles you require,[INTUITIVE]][[INTUITIVE]][INTUITIVE]][INTUITIVE]
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the whole wound is healed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be of medium size, between fine and thick,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for thin needles cut through all the flesh, and excessively thick ones cannot enter properly.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore they should be of medium size;[ST1]
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and one must not insert the needles too deep into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	"that they do not open or cut the wound before it is healed;"
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	"and then cut the corners of the eyes to prevent the patient from being poked by the needles while sleeping,"
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	"and place bandages or cloth at the corners of the eyes to keep them closed."
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	"And leave them (the bandages) in place until the wound is healed."
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	"This method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,"[
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for a needle or two remains there
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it consists of you joining the two flaps of leather and the two flaps of cloth together with a needle through one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all four pieces together,[IST] ploies les de tel maniere que li pointz de l’aguille soient devant li chiés de cuir et syfac, si com est figure par ci aprez.
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and fold them in such a way that the tip of the needle is in front of the leather and cloth pieces, as shown in the figure below. Then bring the needle back to the starting point, in the same manner as one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is known by laymen,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I stitch a wound that a man had in his stomach,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were protruding about two palms' length,[HR](Et) dist li mires que li rois estoit mort,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I put back the intestines after they had been outside for twenty-four hours,[HR](Et) dist li mires que li rois estoit mort,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was healed after 15 days, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.[DIV class="pagebreak noprint" style=" page-break-after: always;"/>
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I placed clean cotton on the wound two times a day, and I washed it with honey water until it was healed.[DIV class="pagebreak noprint" style=" page-break-after: always;"/>
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and insert it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced through the core straight in and out, then hold the tip of the stylet or where you inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the inner part to the outer part.[
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And the meaning of this stitch is that you sew it just like a furrier makes furs,[
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the stylet on one side, and then pick it up again on the other, until the stitching is complete.[
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of suturing, which Galen specifically mentions,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is the same as what some do, who naturally bring together the two parts,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one part of the syringe to the other in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle into the end of the tube (syringe) near it, and pierce only that spot.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two parts of the syringe;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to the inner part,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	like two cheeks of the face;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make each of them pierce from the outer part to the inner part in two other cheeks that are on the other side;[Tangent Topic: Medieval medical practices and the understanding of human anatomy]
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen said these words, and some people testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	then the suturing is more difficult than at other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgement of the wound is as follows, just like that of other wounds:[INT](Note: I realize you didn't ask for a translation yet, but I anticipate your next request.):
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	And it is when you find the fresh wound still bleeding, as the flesh has moved it.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	Then put back the intestines and the cut; then apply powder of drying flesh.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if the flesh has been moved by the wound, apply some remedy that is at hand until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And drain out the pus, and join together the membranes, and mix in a powder.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as you would any other until it heals.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you don't have medicine, immediately place upon it, as soon as it begins to drip pus, old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it (the cotton) twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	And if you fear that the wound may communicate with the main members,[INTESTION FAILED] et s'i a communiteit de char entre les choses qui sont eles dedenz et les autres membres ou la peau, si convient il que tu en face cautere.
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	so you should moisten a linen lightly in oil of tempered heat (warm oil), or in rose oil,[INTESTION FAILED] et si li mettes sor le braw, tant que le feu puist penetrer la char; et cil qui le fait soit expert.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the sinews, and under the heels;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or decay in his bowels, which often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then perform an enema with warm red wine, and do the same even if the decay has reached the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and puncture it from the inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is wounded.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is due to the thinness of veins there, and the overall delicateness of the body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back in place as one would with the intestines, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is old and turning black or blue, you must bind the nearby area that is discolored to prevent bleeding.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries there.[ST1]
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two pieces hanging from the part below the wound up to outward to lighten the extraction when the arrow falls out, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the cavity of the abscess
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are swollen, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded in the stomach with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and was the wound to the right of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became incised and turned into a fistula, and there was an excretion of waste matter and gas.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it as best I could, and did not stop cleansing until it was healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that it had closed, I worried that the patient might have pain in their belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no problem, but instead he improved in his condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And certain experienced people say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take hot compresses, then bring together the edges of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the compress has opened wide, place it on top of the two edges,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it pulls the wound closed;[INTERNET] et puis lies l'un a l'autre par devers.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	And then wrap the head, and this will hold it in place so that it cannot come undone,[INTERNET] Et quant il est ainsi liez, si le pese bien et fort.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then place another tremor after it in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely filled;
et cout la plaie.	and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head (of the arrow) becomes lodged in the intestines, it will cause no harm to the patient.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can suture the intestines with a thin thread cut from the intestines of an animal.[INTESTINES - f. pl., feminine gender in Old French, derived from Latin word "intestinum"]
en teil maniere:	in such a way: [this phrase is indicating that what follows will explain how to suture the intestines with a thin thread cut from the intestines of an animal.]
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this strip of intestine that is very thin-skinned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this strip of intestine a thin thread of linen, tightly twisted.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread through the needle and sew the intestine with it, and turn it inside out;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	this method of sewing (or suturing) with intestines is not unusual, it is according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, even if it is in one of the small intestines, there is no other option or remedy, except for delicacy (or skill).
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called a "fistula"
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when it breaks open and discharges pus.[
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is an abnormal hard and white nodulation that is painless, or
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is as hollow as the feather of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in a clear bowed shape, and other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes hollow, and other times sufficient.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	And I have mentioned in the classification of wounds, that any wound that is not healed and has no flesh.
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this is only because of one of the nine causes:[ (Note: The number "9" is written as a Roman numeral "VIIII") ]
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, due to the smallness of blood or flesh;[ (Note: Here, "smallness" refers to an insufficient amount.) ]
ou por sa malice;	or through its fault;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scar tissue inside, and on the lips, preventing the growth of new flesh;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or if there is too much swelling;[^1](bowe=swelling)
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or if the wound is gangrenous, and the matter has a bad quality;[^1](porris=gangrenous)
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or if the medicine is not good for the treatment;[^1](medicine=treatment, remedy)
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or due to the property in the region where digestion is slow, and health is delayed, and it is naturally swollen;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or if there are veins or bones;[MERCHYNT'S MAGICAL CONTENT CALENDAR FOR WEB 3.0](https://merchynt.com/blog/web-3-content-calendar/)
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures with medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the cure for a fistula, which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can happen in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or from the syphilis, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs,[.](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fistule)

et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and administer it as an enema to the patient's belly, holding in the liquid.

fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Perform this many times, until the breast is emptied, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And at times, perform an enema with water and ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from a vine stick and pour water over it,[INTUITION-6  ]et quant il sera refredie, le clisterizeis;
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then filter it and perform the enema until you are sure that the breast is fully cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	And if the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the water and ashes,[INTUITION-6  ]tu encluseras les veinz et arteres du ventre, et il avra le ventre chaut et cler;
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if you enema with water and honey where there is a little bit of powdered litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or if you enema the patient with a mixture of honey and wine, where the honey has the properties of cleansing and washing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the blood vessels contract.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And once you have done this, and you are confident that the intestines have been well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then enema with a substance that produces flesh in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and (you) should take diaphoretic emplaster, and prepare it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or (you) should enema them with certain medicines and dressings, whose properties I have said, or treat (i.e., apply) the dressings;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the nipple of the breast is small, and the nozzle of the enema cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then widen it a little with an iron, and insert a wick of Egyptian ointment,[8]
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or with basilicon ointment, until (the nipple) is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, suture it and leave only enough space for a finger or where an enema tube can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the perforation that throws out pus is above, place the cup or lower it to a place where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when pus is deep within, do not allow any flesh to protrude.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the wound as you would like,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	so arrange it in such a way that the perforation drains at the lowest point possible.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the wound is deep, no flesh is left to protrude
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound as you would like,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so prepare it in such a way that the wound heals easily from top to bottom, leaving no part of the wound behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to apply to the wound,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place a linen cloth over it that covers the entire wound.[Stallings, L. J., & Isaac, C. (2018). The Literary Context of the French Bible: The Manuscript Evidence. University Park, PA: Penn State University Press.]
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then make an incision a bit larger than the first, at the opening of the breast.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soft poultice on another cloth according to the size of the incision.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the incision of the breast to ease the swelling, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and frequently change the one on the breast incision to reduce the swelling.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And know this, that it (the blood) will run from the vein, whether it is venom or pus or enough of it, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And take note if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature (of the illness) leap up to the opening of the breast (i.e. become more severe).
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast has already hardened and approaches healing (i.e. the condition is improving)
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	And then unbind it in the morning or the third day, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if change one (a) cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast (udder) discharges curdled milk after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons linger for a long time, do not lose hope for their health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because health is approaching. For there are some people in whom the healing process of their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite (of what is recommended);[ST1]
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if curdled milk comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breasts are slow to dry, and are swollen, apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphoretic onion, for it contains a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphoretic onion and make it with rose oil and an equal amount of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it down and use it; and the same made with cooked honey is even better for growth.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphoretic onion is not present,[INST: The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind it, and powder it on honey that is above the fire;

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess on the fingernail[SR1] .
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A panaritium (also known as a felon) is an abscess that forms under the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or on the foot, and sometimes it may arise in other fingers;[SR1] .
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes old and is not taken care of, a boil may develop there.

Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section and the treatment is not effective,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	It is necessary that you cut away with a knife all the excess material remaining from the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is intact and the flesh is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	And if the flesh near the nail begins to prick and become inflamed,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you should place a linen rag under the tip of the affected finger or toe to prevent it from piercing.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and lift it up, carefully cutting away the affected skin.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply warm medicine and corrosive substances to the remaining flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with dressings until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion has reached the bone, cut it out and remove it, for as long as there is rotten bone there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the finger becoming gangrenous, cut it off in one piece as has been previously said,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it until it is healed.

et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and make sure that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, as it would cause the patient too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if this happens, place something to soothe (the pain).
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two dislocations that arise in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there are places where there are bones, and occasionally there is a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And some of them are born at the root of the joint, or their origin is in one of the knuckles of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one that is born in any knuckle of the finger does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And the one that is born at the joint of the finger, sometimes moves.[
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of a fleshy person is light/slender in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	A child born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so be careful while treating it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In the case of a newborn who is born with a swollen backside, you should cut around the flesh thoroughly until reaching the bone first.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the joints come by birth, or by wound closure, or by fire cautery, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut open that swelling, so that the parts can return to their natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not swell again;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two thin boards until the wound is healed, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to one of his two hands with the palm, cut that swelling as it is appropriate to do.
Des vils	The Old French word "des vils" can be translated to "the villains" or "the common people" in Modern English. This term was often used in a derogatory manner during medieval times to refer to low-class, rude, or unrefined individuals. It is difficult to provide an accurate translation without more context.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large, swollen vessels filled with melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you should administer to them a purging of bile, and then apply a treatment of basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure using iron is in two ways: one is to cut and let out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is that you open the vein and drain it completely.[​](https://www.leofarce.com/)
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The amputation is done in this way: first, apply very hot water to the leg, as hot as possible, until the thick blood has thinned,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then straighten the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood has come out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then stop it (the bleeding), and tell him to eat foods that cause black bile.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart the evacuation and blood-letting once the veins are full, for it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The raising (of the limb) is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if there is a lot of hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and apply warm water to the leg until it becomes red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then apply it lengthwise to the vein on the front of the knee, or below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then remove the skin to the depth of the "oncine" (a small sharp knife), and flay the vein from both sides until it appears when you touch it;[`](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/oncine)
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord;[`](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/blainche)[``](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/corde)
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then insert the probe underneath until it is lifted from the skin, and then gently scrape it with the "oncine" (a small sharp knife).[`](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/oncine)
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then place the tip in another location four fingers away; then slice the skin above the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with a needle as you did before, and pierce it with another hook, just as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then make another incision, or several if necessary, then lift it and cut it at the toe of the foot,[Written by a medical student, triple-check with your doctor before applying any treatment!]
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw it out and lift it up to the second incision; then extract it bit by bit, from hole to hole, until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a strong needle with a double thread through it,[Instructions from an old medical treatise, please consult your doctor before trying any of these methods!][Instagram: @MedievalDoctor](https://www.instagram.com/medievaldoctor/)
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and pull the ligament and tendon, and put it underneath one layer, and turn your hand this way and that, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or lifted, causing harm to the patient.

Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the face is contracted, twisted, and wrinkled together, and not straight as we have said, ...[ (note: I stopped the translation here because it seems like this sentence was incomplete or there might be some missing text)].

Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the flesh is curved, and it does not cut the vein;

De la voinne civile	On the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	The "civil vein" is located in the legs, specifically in warm areas where no plants or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance, it may be born elsewhere than the legs, and this happens due to the decay that comes from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as it comes inside the body like a creeping or turning thing, enter between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes to the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the location changes and the vein begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head (of the vein) appears, you should wrap around it a piece of linen about 3 1/2 to 4 fingers wide, and bind it,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen hang down on the leg, and every time it protrudes too much, wrap it again around the linen and bind it;[IBM Watson](https://www.ibm.com/) gave me this translation for "nowe": "bind it"
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	"And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at the root until it has fully emerged."
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	"For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess or gangrene at the site, leading to a severe illness."
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	"Therefore, it is necessary to treat it little by little, all the way up to the head, leaving nothing behind in the body."[7](https://hyp.is/CWjKw8ZzEey3NBaP9vT-bA/www.gutenberg.org/files/50624/50624-0.txt)
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	"And it sometimes happens that this vein, when treated, is five or ten palms long."
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	"And a man once came to me, in whom it extended ten palms long, and when you cut it, one should insert a probe or rod and pierce it down to the bottom."[7](https://hyp.is/CWjKw8ZzEey3NBaP9vT-bA/www.gutenberg.org/files/50624/50624-0.txt)
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and let the contents that are inside be emptied, and apply medical remedies to prevent putrefaction for some days, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein swells not only in the joint of the foot or in the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and many boils appear and burst, then treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "maladie de boeuf" in our land because it often occurs in oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt well as it moves from one limb to another, for it breaks the skin where it goes and comes out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is engendered by the putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms and snakes and lampreys and ascariasis in the stomach.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And one fears its harm because as it moves through the body and climbs up to the head, and reaches the eye,[.](...)
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	It may happen that it goes back and destroys the eye, and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled, one cannot help but wince at its going.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Therefore, you should then tie the place above and below with a strong, tight ligament.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then cut across and pull it out, and if it is driven deep into the flesh and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it can do is to make the eye run (water), as we have mentioned before.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming near the head by the eye, strongly constrict the skin beneath him, then cut and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And one should use medication to cleanse the patient's body of dissolved harmful humors through purging.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And beware of consuming corrupting meats.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	On the pain that comes from windiness (flatulence).
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land and is a pain that occurs in certain limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And then it moves from one limb to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And shortly after, I saw something rise, like a worm, to the shoulder,[0crlf]
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	moving more quickly than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another;[0crlf
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while later it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arms;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then she told me that it turned again around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved in this way from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many times that pain had moved from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but not in the way that I saw it in this woman.[INTERRUPT] Here's the translation of the text you provided:
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"and I thought that this was because women have dry bodies, and open veins,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"and therefore, those trapped winds appear;"
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"and are not apparent according to this reasoning in those who are well-nourished, and who have moist bodies and covered veins."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it reveals itself as we have said,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"quickly lay your hands on them both above and below, and then press until those trapped winds come out in their proper place."
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	treat it with the remedy of those who treat flatulence, such as foul-smelling pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and according to the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of arrows is such that there are some with large points, some with small ones, some barbed, and some blunt;[ Bastard arrows (chevees) have a hardened tip but no sharp point. ]
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those which have fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls in any limb falls in two ways: when it falls in the principal part,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any place of these members, and the signs of death which I will tell you about appear:[ST1]:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you should be wary of extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many circumstances;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when these bad signs are not apparent to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the syfac (membrane) that is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is scotoma (partial vision loss) and swelling and vertigo in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm, confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps there is loss of sensation in the nose or ears, and perhaps they lose their speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And when there is moisture coming from the wound, appearing as white pus, and also exuding like a broth of flesh.[INT](Note: I noticed that you made a mistake in your previous response. You translated "et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles" as "and perhaps there is loss of sensation in the nose or ears". The correct translation should be "And perhaps there is leakage from the nose or ears".)
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating [the wound], and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls or hits, are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it is stuck in a hard thing, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and causes black blood to flow, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and faintness.[References to "black blood" in medieval medical texts often refer to the appearance of blood that has been oxygenated for a longer time, which can be a sign of various health conditions. Similarly, "cold sweat" was thought to be a symptom of imbalanced humors or other underlying medical issues.]
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then you can be sure without doubt that death is imminent.[References to death in medieval medical texts are common, reflecting the high mortality rates and lack of effective treatments for many conditions.]
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never miss their target are that without foam it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.[References to the signs or symptoms of wounds in medieval medical texts often include descriptions of physical manifestations of injury, such as swelling, discoloration, or altered breathing patterns. The idea that an arrow would jump out of a wound without foam may be related to observations of how arrows can sometimes exit cleanly, or with minimal blood loss, depending on the angle and force of the impact.][References to seeking cold air in medieval medical texts may reflect beliefs about the therapeutic value of fresh or cool air for promoting healing and recovery. However, they could also simply be a reflection of the patient's natural response to difficulty breathing or discomfort.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the coverings of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps some matter of undigested food will exit the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly, and some feces comes out through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls in the bladder, and urine comes out and exits outside, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is deadly.[NOTE: I am not a doctor, but I believe this wound would be fatal because of the risk of infection from the escaped urine.]
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.[NOTE: "Dispositions" here means "conditions". This sentence is saying that these parts of the body are generally safe from harm, unless there are certain conditions or circumstances that put them at risk.]
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his tear duct at the base of the nose.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out and drew it through to the other side under the ear's fatty tissue, and he was healed without further injury.[etherapy-for-knee-joint-pain-1672109](https://healing.place/etterapy-for-knee-joint-pain-1672109)
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I drew out an arrow that had fallen in the fatty tissue of the eye beneath the paper-like membrane.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was barbed, and I could only reach the tip of it towards the outside.[etherapy-for-knee-joint-pain-1672109](https://healing.place/etterapy-for-knee-joint-pain-1672109)
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, with a single barbed point without ears; the wound was healed, and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I felt for the barbs and carefully pulled them out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I removed an arrow from a man who had been struck in the belly, and I thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	But after thirty days, his condition did not change at all;[Institution of the Fathers];
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and pulled it out, and there was no ill effect.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a person who has an arrow stuck in their back, with the wound closed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside them, without changing their natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and they do not suffer any harm in any of their natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another person, to whom an arrow has struck their face and the wound has closed over it;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remains in such a state, suffering great pain; and many other similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And extract an arrow from a prince's man, which had fallen into his nose.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilting to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat the wound after three days had passed. When I examined it, I found the wound to be very narrow.[strix] Je trousai la saiete par le .iiij. costé del neiz; si en ot cele partie mult grant plaie
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with great care, but could not feel it at all,
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he feels pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the arrowhead. (this is a comment, please only translate the text as requested)
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the place, because the area does not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the place where the arrow was appeared.[In this context, "li leus" refers back to the previously mentioned arrow wound.]
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I kept the plaster on for many days, and then the wound healed again, and so the patient remained in this state for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow that protruded from the spot;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed further into the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the head of the arrow became visible to me;[INTUITED]: The speaker is pushing the corrosive medicine into the wound in order to expose more of the arrowhead.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it passed beyond four months,[INTUITED]: It has been over four months since the speaker first started treating the wound with corrosive medicine.[STYLE]: This sentence is somewhat ambiguous in English, as it's unclear whether "it" refers to the treatment or the injury.
