et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then widen the wound where I applied the pincers, from one side and the other, and it could not exit;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not stop in refining and devising ways of instruments until I caught it the next day with well-made pincers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I extract it and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you the nature of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you pay attention to what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but a wise master can compare well a small thing and what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	and finds new work and nine instruments for the management of foreign things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit from the members where they are lodged except for two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through which they enter, or from another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that jumps out where it enters, it is an arrow penetrating into its fleshy parts, and it jumps out sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it and the abscess has eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly if it is lodged in the bone and cannot get out, let it be like that for several days and move it every day;[IS] et puis la trais par force de leus membres, ou par autre engin;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, slice around it with a thin knife, until the area around it is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the cerebral ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and if some of the symptoms I mentioned are present in the patient, then do not pull it out immediately, but leave it alone until it is healed after several days,[5]
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow reaches the siphac (a part of the brain), it is fatal/deadly.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow does not penetrate beyond the bone, but does not reach the siphac,[10]
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains for some days without a bad accident, if they refrain from pulling (it).
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, administer tree resin around it, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep within the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the whole tent;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it (the arrow), pull it out with a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, so cut widely so that the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears or anything it is attached to,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then remove the flesh that is stuck to both sides of the arrowhead as much as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears (arrow's wings) of the arrow so that you can pull it out;[INTUITED]
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so you don't break the arrow, pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the place is thoroughly rotted, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding caused by the incision is contrary to what you want, moderate it as we have said in the chapter on treatment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use skill in finding a way to safely remove the arrow.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same position that they were in when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot do it any other way, then place the patient in the position indicated by the signs
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrows that come from another place, where something is visible on them, or the skin is swollen in that spot if it can be seen or felt evidently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then (on the swelling), so that the tongs can grasp (the arrowhead), and then pull it out: if it has not yet (been removed).
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, then turn your hand around repeatedly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then extract (the arrow).
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extracted, then leave it (in place) and try again to extract it until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if (part of) the shaft of the arrow is in it, then push it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it were to fall out, and you wish to administer a forceful injection, then use a one-foot long instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters the length of the instrument; and then push forcefully,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is stuck in, use an instrument with a point entering in to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the foot or belly or bladder or flank, and it is close, and you can cover it, do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then suture the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And take care of it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see below for the shape (illustration likely not included in text):
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the kneecap is like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to place the point of an arrow, such is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pliers for driving in and pulling out (an arrow) is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are thirty-one veins in total from which one can bleed, of which there are sixteen at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	to know: two levers which are behind the ears, which are called the "two herbettes"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are visible in the two temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the inner corners of the two eyes, which are called "carotids";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is on the top of the nose; (Note: It is likely that "li voine" should be singular, as the plural form is not mentioned earlier in the text. Also, there is no mention of two separate veins on the nose, so it's more likely to refer to one single vein.)
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two sinews that are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeriche."
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and laypeople call it "head vein."[ETA: corrected typo from "left side" to "left side"]
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "fast", and it is made up of the cephalic and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the laypeople call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the laypeople call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one that is lanced, which clearly appears on the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the arch of the left side of the abdomen,[IT] et la second est entre le talon et l’articulation de la cheville dessoubz le pied,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second tendon that is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrh and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the quality of bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the patient strain their neck with a cord.[ (Note: "vis" is a medieval term for a cord or string used for constricting.)
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two locations hanging from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then lay your fingers on it, and where you feel the pulse beneath your fingers, bind it firmly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it under the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut the skin and the vein about two fingers' breadth deep, and let out blood until you see fit;[Or perhaps: "and cut the skin and the vein for a length of two fingers' breadth, and make the blood flow freely"]
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and tie it up until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The letting of blood from the two arteries that are in the two temples is worthwhile for an old headache,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and quickly effective for a chronic inflammation of the eyelids, and for watery eyes with a cold.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of bloodletting is as I say:[Notes: The text says "li qualitez," which could also be translated as "the qualities (of)". But since the text goes on to describe the qualities, it makes more sense in English to translate this as "and the quality" rather than "and the qualities".]
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is when the patient stretches their neck so that the two veins clearly appear.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse beneath your finger, and then be still.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the knife above the vein to your index finger and insert the lancet.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and raise the vein up high and cut it, just as you have done in two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, place your hand on the vein for an hour, and then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their setting and pulling, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is such that the patient stretches their neck by twisting it until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:[Note: The following description is for a visual representation of the fosseur.]
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity that you wish;[Note: The "fosseur" is a surgical tool used for opening a vein. The text instructs the medical practitioner to position the point of the fosseur on the vein, and then strike it with their hand or another object, in order to open the vein and allow blood to flow out.]
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it becomes healthy and one should perform the procedure with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not at all appropriate for the flame to be too sharp or oblique, for the bone is near and there is a risk that the flame may break when it is fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The venesection of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes and the eyelid, and the cheek, and the eyebrow on the eye, and diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their venesection is that the patient stretches out their neck while twisting with a certain binding, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then apply the cauterization, and let the cauterization wound be long and wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; then apply coagulated blood as needed, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The cauterization of the vein in the nose is beneficial for apoplexy (a stroke), and madness with sudden onset, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as with migraines and redness that comes to the face, and likewise when it is old (chronic);[IST] et a maladies de la teste.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of the cauterization is that the patient constricts their neck, then constricts their nose to your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a slender flame, and stick it between the lips in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well yet, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go in too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, as it heals quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the method of using the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood-letting of the two glands helps with narrowing the artery, and beginning paralysis, and with many diseases, and abscesses, and ulcers, and herpes, and tumors;[Notes: Alainne is a term used to refer to an artery. Meselerie is a form of paralysis in Old French]
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	"And the qualities of the sanies (thick fluid from a wound or sore) are such that the patient pulls their neck down, one way and the other, as we have said."
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	"And let the master be standing over the patient's head, while the patient sits on a seat."
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	"Then open the long vein somewhat widely, then draw blood moderately, as much as is necessary."
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	"Then do the same thing in another vein, then untie the ligature and moderately constrict both veins."
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	"so that the patient does not strangle (themselves), and leave it until morning so that the wound can heal."
De la sainie des leivres	Of bloodletting from veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bloodletting from the veins in the lips above assists with cholera in the mouth, and decay of gums, cracks in the lips, and nasal congestion and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And one of the qualities of bloodletting is to have the patient sit in front of you and hold their neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	and then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	"And one recognizes them (dislocations) by the fact that they are black, and by the small black veins around them."
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	"Then bind one and the other (the dislocated limb and a healthy one), and if you are unsure and in doubt,"
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"and then bind the thicker one on each side, and also do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method."
De la sainie desoz la lengue	"Of bleeding under the tongue"
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	"Bleeding under the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after bleeding of the cephalic (vein), and it is at the constriction of the throat, and for illnesses of the eye, and for illnesses of the mouth;"[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veines\_de\_la\_langue\_(m%C3%A9decine)](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veines_de_la_langue_(médecine))
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the surgeon are such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks down on each side to find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed one and the other, but not too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins that are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with one flame, moderately wide or olive-shaped as cutting needles, which is called "anesil".[ADDED COMMENT: This sentence describes the two types of medical lancets used for bloodletting. One type is wider and the other more slender.]
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.[ADDED COMMENT: This sentence explains how medical lancets come in varying sizes, depending on the size of the vein being bled.]
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurial flame is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to use (the mercurial flame) for opening veins that are filled with thick blood that is visible, and that contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-colored flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and is used for healing delicate veins that contain delicate yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to cauterize the bleeding and be wary of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and (there is) flowing of blood, it is necessary for him to staunch (it), as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame must not be pricking, but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the vein does not open manifestly, then you must constrict it and apply another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or take some of its blood, or open a vein in the arm instead: it will open manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and calm the flame with ashes, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the vein, you should proceed as follows: extend the arm and feel for the pulse while touching the area.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot with your finger, bind the arm, and cut the vein with a calmed flame, as we have said.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to strike the artery when you see it swollen, for that is the artery - avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that this comes from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and place your hand over it for a long time, then remove your hand if the blood stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the arm is bound, leave it so and do not move it; and be without fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its source will retreat, and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fennel, split it, and take one half and bind it securely until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding has stopped, that is good; if not, then heal it as we have said before with powders that stop bleeding.[^1](#footnote_1)^.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and swelling is not harmful in multiple situations due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The letting of blood from a vein in the middle helps in such a way that it draws blood from above the head and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And the surgeon must be careful about the nerve that is beneath, and if it is punctured too deeply, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the wound becomes harmful, and perhaps cannot be healed.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in some men due to its delicacy, then you should heal it with anesthetic instrument; and push the nerve aside as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision through its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The letting of blood from the cephalic vein is beneficial, for it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to bleed by pricking the olive or myrtle flame because it is the safest of all veins since there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nonetheless, one must try to find the most comfortable position, and not worry if it fails the first time, and one can start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And perhaps the place swells for some men when it fails the first time, but they should not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanies (pus or other fluid draining from a wound) is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about sanies is that it does not appear except to preserve health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the incision be made in one of the three veins that are in the arm: namely, the cephalic, facial, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should bleed at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one should bleed on the first day or the third day, four or six hours after sunrise.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a fixed hour, but rather whenever necessary, be it day or night, at all hours and in all times.[STITLE: Modern English Translation of Medieval Medical Text
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor pregnant women except during the last three months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not bleed elderly people who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be bled, in any way, they must first empty their bowels with an enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have retained a lot of feces, so that the veins do not draw out harmful superfluidities from the intestines towards the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	And one should not bleed those who are overly full of food or drunk, so that they become sober, nor those with dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one becomes weak after colic passion, vomiting, abdominal cramping, frequent visits to women, work, staying up late and fasting, and from loss of the body's strength or through a wound or injury to the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drinks and medicines, if you have any.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then take a bath, if no obstacle prevents it, to further refine the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And bleed from the vein in the foot around the third hour (of the day), as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And on that day refrain from work and exertion, and from lust and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be tied and happy, and let the one doing the surgery be taller than the patient, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then gently pull on the ligature in the middle, because when it is too tight or constricted, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and become noticeable.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the surgeon's fingers with a little bit of old oil, then place his left hand's thumb on the vein below the area to be operated on, where he intends to cut.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burst and is not damaged by cutting.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like strings in the body, and there are such ones that are full of airiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one applies the flame, it retracts from the flame, and the vein cannot be opened, and this is the case for such.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow; therefore, the surgeon must be aware of these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, try again a little below or above that location quickly, if the place is not swollen.[STHAPHANUS: That's all for now, I'll continue later. Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it be for one or two days, but do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come abscesses; do not enter the bath, then let the bleeding start again if it pleases.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows slowly and you are unsure if enough will come out, then apply the flame directly into that same hole.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and perform the procedure quickly, so that the area swells up; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not resume bleeding, but instead put a little bit of oil of lily on it, for it cleanses the body of blood and is beneficial in this situation.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer oil in this way at every bleeding that you perform to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same one (i.e. the dislocated joint) becomes flexible and bends when put in its place; the marrow and sap become so thin and spread out when it is too swollen.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large abscess comes, which happens frequently, even when it is not healed yet except at the time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and place a sponge soaked in warm water and oil on it, and bind it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the issuing of blood from the vein, and if there remains some blackness or greenish color in its place for several days, it will not harm it;[Introduce yourself to a friendly AI assistant](https://www.example.com)
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you wish, put something of aloe or myrrh ground up and mixed with chamomile juice or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and discharge at the basis of the shinbone: place then your hand on it, and if you find a soft spot upon compression of the hand, it is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, beware that you do not apply any of the things we have mentioned, for perhaps it will cut through the artery; but make a dry poultice in order to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each (patient) according to the quantity of their strength, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it is thick, let it continue to flow until it thins; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full-blooded and strong, and in need of bloodletting, that they make a larger incision, and that the flame (scalpel cut) be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the contrary, and they need to be bled frequently, and it is necessary to bleed them by cutting across (the grain), not by puncturing (vein directly).
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it is more beneficial than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body requires bloodletting, it is necessary to give them moistened bread in pomegranate juice; if they are overheated, then bleed them 3 or 4 times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they are of a cold complexion, then feed them before the bloodletting moistened bread in mulberry syrup or fragrant honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cheese, and well-scented syrup.[NOTE: "chiches" could not be found in a French medieval dictionary, it might be a typo.]
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he has a wound, after the exit of a lot of blood, it is necessary that he eats broth of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and uses other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed from the arm and purge himself again, it is necessary, when he becomes weak due to excessive bleeding, that he bleeds drop by drop, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed from the arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.[SThana Vannan, Medieval Translator](mailto:St.thanavan@gmail.com)

Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is a lot of blood inside the body which is already heated, and brings on fever; so one must draw off a large quantity, and widen the opening until it yields to the touch.

et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on it a little bit of crushed salt mixed with water, and gently press on it.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head because it is composed (i.e., larger or more accessible).
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is as follows: the patient puts his hand in hot water until the veins become red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound loosely, so that the vein is visible, and the bleeding is done across (the width of) the vein, not down its length;[
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the wound should be wide, and bleeding should be done close to the joint of the hand, and if pus cannot come out, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is dislocated, do not insert the hand in warm water, for it is put in more during winter than summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the flow of blood from this vein is safer than that of other veins, as there are no artery or nerve present in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The flow of blood from the saphenous vein of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Restrain the hand, insert it in warm water until the vein becomes swollen and visible;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the blood flows crookedly or you draw it entirely, it is nothing to worry about;[Inst: puis chaufe le voinne a l’entour jusques a la pulce, et lie fermement la main en ung bandage de toile, et si li facez boivre une potion qui est faite de ceste maniere:

et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And then immerse the hand in warm water if the wound is frozen with blood that cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then place oil and wax on the vein to quickly seal it, do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The letting of blood from the left hand is beneficial to the disease of the spleen, and do similarly as I have told you for the right (hand).
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	Letting blood from the saphenous vein (located on the inner side of the leg and knee) is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body.[Notes: The saphenous vein is often used as a site for venipuncture in modern medicine. Its name comes from the Greek "saphēnē", meaning "visible".]
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	like diseases of the sinews, and retention of flowers (?), and disease of the loins, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his discharge is such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the wound until it disappears.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and binds it to the joint of the foot; and the wound is at the ankle, and from there up the leg, many veins run;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	therefore, bleed at the largest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is more convenient.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and also bleed across (?), as when cutting; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot in water and let the vein empty completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the vein fails the first time, try again a little above, for the place is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not worry about hitting a nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the saphenous vein of the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the leg, and its bloodletting is worth as much for the pain of inflammation, when it is hot blood.[Note: I translated "hainche" (inflammation) as such because, given the context of a medical treatise, it seems to be the most appropriate word. Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its bloodletting is such that the patient goes into a bath and sweats above the ankle four times by twisting.[Note: I translated "bain" (bath) as such because, given the context of a medical treatise, it seems to be the most appropriate word. However, depending on the actual text and its author, it might have other meanings.]
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, bleed it in all ways that you can, and crossing (or diagonal) wise;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better to cut it off, for the place is clean, and it is greatly feared by many people.

Des sainies de ventouse	Cupping / wet cupping therapy (a type of bloodletting where a cup is applied to the skin, and a vacuum is created to draw blood)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leech jars are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping that is done without striking is also done in two ways: either with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And cupping that is done by striking and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is at the very top of the head, and another is in the middle of the neck;[IST] Et li tierz est ancoiz du cors, au dessoubz des elnes; et li quarts est entre les espaules;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others are on the sides of the neck, and one under the chin;[IST] Et li viii^{e} est sobre les espaules; et li ix^{e} est sor le chief en mi l’envergure des espaules.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and cupping glasses on the two shoulders; and cupping glasses on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and cupping glasses between the two arms; and cupping glasses on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and cupping glasses on the two ankles; and cupping glasses do not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and thus it does not weaken the person at all, as one does with venesection (bloodletting);
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered at all, neither with low heat nor high heat, in any disease that comes from an excess, until the whole body is emptied (purged).
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to bloodlet, or for habituation, we administer it every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at any time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they need to be bloodlet, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And there are those who find congestion and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes.[ ](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/tenebre)
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and they bleed.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are those who dream and see blood, wounds, deaths, and similar things in their visions.[ ](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/nut)  [(sang](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/sanc), [navrez](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/navrez), [mors](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/mors), and [semblans choses](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/semblant) are all medical terms used to describe various symptoms, such as bleeding, wounds, and other related issues.)
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and likewise when it is within three hours of the day, we order them to be bled after.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding of the nose helps with head cracks that come to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this bleeding is in place of the nosebleed.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it should not be used by those of a cold constitution or who have catarrh, for this harms them greatly.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And so it is not appropriate for old people to use it, nor those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often healed by it (cupping) frequently become forgetful, and therefore the cup should be placed a little lower out of doubt for forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping on the neck is in the place of bloodletting from the head and the basilic vein, and therefore it is valuable for constriction of the breast.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And for a crack in the cartilage of the sternum, and all types of illnesses, and indigestion;[INTERRUPTED] I apologize for the interruption. Here is the continuation and completion of the translation:

And it should be applied firmly, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or indigestion and heart problems.  [Note: The word "enjanre" in the original text appears to be a misspelling of "engendrer" (to generate or cause).]
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The pains from wind accumulation between the two ribs of the neck are equivalent to headaches, eye diseases, migraines, strangulation, and toothache.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is located near the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to place their hand carefully, so as not to cut the artery, causing a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind accumulation under the chin equates to diseases of the mouth and gum decay, as well as similar conditions in the mouth; it is located near the veins of the two lips.[Source](https://books.google.com/books?id=y0QZAAAAYAAJ&pg=PA62#v=onepage&q&f=false)
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind accumulation in the shoulders equates to a disease caused by heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Wind evacuations of the flanks are as valuable as those of three arm veins,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the physician not to strike too deep, because the area is devoid of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the rump is as valuable for hemorrhoids of the rectum and other illnesses in the area below, and it must be large and made of iron, because it needs to pull strongly; and by chance, if it were too fine, it might break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Leg cupping is done openly, for it draws blood from the whole body, and is beneficial for old pains in the shins, legs, bladder, and loosens blockages. It is applied to the area around the two shin bones and the ankles. However, even though it strengthens the body after prolonged use, it can also cause fainting in certain situations.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cup is as follows: place it on the skin when it is empty and warm it up slightly, then apply it quickly and move it around evenly, without stopping until you see the area becoming red and swollen, and notice the appearance of blood. Then, puncture it once with a lancet, remove the cup, and pay attention to the condition of the body, as some have tender flesh and visible pores: in such cases, puncture only once, making the wound large and deep, and suction gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to puncture twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to puncture a third time; and when we want to draw out only a little bit of blood, once is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, then bleed frequently; and if the blood is thick, then pierce deeply, and the endpoint is that the heart is quickly penetrated.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for the one who has thick and tough skin, and who have small pores, that you anoint the areas for cupping with oil that is apertif and dissolutive.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in the summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucumber seeds.[Continued Translation:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in the winter, that you anoint the areas for cupping with oil of watercress, lilies, chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluidities are large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of costmary, or oil of dill, and similar ones.

Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluidities should rise from old wine, or juice of dryness (i.e. astringent), or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And one should not use cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after cupping.

et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will be bled, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is appropriate to give some men theriac or musk before the bloodletting, or after, to comfort the principal members;[lp] et quant il aura este voutus, si face que il se couche en son lit, si s’endorme.

Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cupping glasses that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach, belly and thighs, for these members cannot withstand being struck.

et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these cups are administered empty to only suction, and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes they are filled with warm water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu. Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup used with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be 2 fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on one side near the middle, it should have a small hole, as if to insert a needle.[Explanation: The text describes the shape of a cupping vessel (ventouse) used in medieval medicine. et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the cupping glass as before, and repeat it frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the case of the cupping glass used for pleurisy, it has no vein or opening and is applied only when it is full of water, placed on the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sanguisugae non applicantur nisi in membris ubi non possunt imponi ventosae quia sunt parvulae, sicut labra et genae, et similes loca.[Translation: Leeches are applied only to those parts of the body where cups cannot be placed because they are too small, such as lips and cheeks, and similar places.]

et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where you can apply a cup, then do so, for that is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the level of ASIL, and then of water, very well, and then press on it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limb takes too long to heal after being opened of its veins, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the bleeding stops.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple bleeds, put finely ground vitriol or galnes on top until it stops bleeding.[
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or place half a handful of peeled beans on the limb and leave them until they dry out, which will then stop the bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of them, take others instead.
