Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it concerns the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish surgeons who ignore this chapter have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read (them).
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this, the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found anyone skilled in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have become proficient in it, and also through experience and habit from my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described for you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in the two chapters preceding this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Then it is necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his attention, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to someone, then it is necessary to quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of the body, children, or the elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and eat only lean foods, that is to say cold games such as bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with food which fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that there is no danger of a hot abscess or spreading of matter in the limb; so let the patient return to their original diet and regimen that they were used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for thick nutrition, or have a viscous quality, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and tripe of cattle, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at times, during the setting, movement and healing are sped up and the fracture occurs more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or knit together properly due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not worry, set a large splint on the broken bone which pulls and joins the limb together until it heals as it was before; and do not neglect your work, and therefore you must nourish it with rich foods, as we have said.[Read More](https://medium.com/@healinglanguagehq/old-french-medical-text-translation-4-a0583719e2b)
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse and varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different than that of the hip or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.[Read More](https://medium.com/@healinglanguagehq/old-french-medical-text-translation-5-e81b65904a7)
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another one sharpening, like the split of a pen's nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that is a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own tool and proper instrument in restoration, according to what comes to mind.[Note: This translation is meant to be close to the original text's meaning, but there might be different interpretations of this sentence. The meaning of "ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu" could be ambiguous.]
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the break in the bone is recognized by the fact that the place is twisted and clearly visible, and it sounds under pressure from the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twistiness or sound upon touching and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break.[Note: The word "tocchier" in Old French means to touch. I translated it as such for better understanding. However, it might also be interpreted as "probe". The meaning of this sentence can change slightly depending on how we interpret "tocchier"]
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can indeed have crookedness, or a fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not at all appropriate to move it with your hand, but instead apply the following mentioned medicines and then bind it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that for breaks in the limb, when the two parts are separated, they must now be aligned equally, so that abscesses do not develop there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess does develop, then let it be for some days, until the abscess subsides.[ST1]
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then align it with the muscle that you can easily and safely move, and know that the healing of this one is easier than the healing of one where there are fragments; then bind it as stated below.[ST1](Note: I assume "li restoration" is a typo for "sa restoration")
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it from two sides, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hands if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you bring together all the fragments in their places as much as you can, and take care that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and align well the two ends of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand to make sure that it seems not quite right; then align it nicely and do not stretch it too much or press on it as those do who cause a hot abscess and constriction in the member through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is healed, make sure to instruct the patient not to move it, whether awake or asleep, turning over, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And see to it that the member is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	Because when it feels any pain, it is not in the right position, and one must arrange it in such a way that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And be careful to set it straight, so as to avoid any twisting when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members (bones) vary in smallness and largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For small members, such as arms and legs and the like, one should wrap fine and soft linen cloths around them;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for those that are large, such as the hips and leg: one should wrap them with a wide and firm band, for the wide band embraces the entire large member and constrains it equally from all sides, so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then place light wadding around it, three or four layers depending on the member, and tighten your hand slightly around the entire band, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break is moved slightly apart.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And loosen the band little by little, as you compress a large part of the healthy area, then take another band and wrap it around the broken member again.[Introductory text omitted for brevity] The surgeon must ensure that they do not make a mistake when counting the number of layers used, and should use a marker to keep track.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part below the break, and gently tighten it, not too hard or too lightly, as we have said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place lint or strips of cloth evenly between the ties, so that it is all even, then bind it with a bandage on top. And then put well-made bandages on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing for the abscess that is warm and reduces swelling, and leave it on for several days.[Document 1: Medieval Medical Treatise in Old French (around 12th-13th centuries)] Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu'il laisse les poilz tant qu'il soient lons et igals; et s'il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu'il ne se muevent tant qu'il naissent. Car en l'ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l'ovrir la voinne, et a l'incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l'estraction des saiettes, et a l'incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors. Quant li chiés de l'ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n'i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. Dislocations est issue d'aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion. puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l'estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu'il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s'il n'i a aposteme ou enfleure. Et s'il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l'enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then apply pressure on the bandages, and they should be half the width of a cane, or made of wood used for making nails, or palm ribs, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the steel/metal bar that one places on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is needed for the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten the steel bars as you did at the first suture, and place a fitting bandage over it, just like on the fracture;[Better translation:]
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and tighten more afterward, less so later; and it is necessary that the bandages be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, and made of soft linen;[A better translation:]
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the bandages are thick, as foolish people often do who make their bindings with twisted ropes of linen thread, this is a great error, for a binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not at all appropriate to have less than two fingers' width of space between each steel bar.  [A better translation:]
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the shards of arrows after being tightened in a healthy place, place under them plugs of linen, or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a break and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to bind all broken limbs with arrows on the first day.[_](id:r86v2o3aokvp)
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Because when the limb is large, arrows should not be applied until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the certainty of a hot abscess appearing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method for ancient poultices to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that clings to the walls of a mill, and thicken it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of the poultice that restores fracture in many ways, and also for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.[_](id:r86v2o3aokvp)
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restores the fracture and dislocation and twisted limb: take three ounces each of alabaster, ladanum, enula campana, asafetida, and gum arabic, and myrrh and aloes, five ounces each; aloe juice, eight ounces; and reduce to a powder, and mix with egg white; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster that is good for twisted limbs: take myrrh and plantain, ten ounces; myrrh and aloes, eight ounces; acacia, six ounces; Armenian bole, ten ounces, and grind well, and infuse with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of plaster for dislocated joints and bones out of their places, and eases the pain that occurs, and is used by surgeons for cutting bone and fractures: take new wool, and moisten it with vinegar and cooked oil, and place on the affected area. This plaster does not heal completely, but it is good for relieving hot abscesses, and removing pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed clover, grind together, and make a plaster. (Note: spelling, measurements, and some plant names have been modernized)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way of applying a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess. Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of bran, of each one part; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger way of applying a plaster, compared to the first one, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of marshmallow, flax seeds, valerian, melilot, and elderflower and violet and chamomile flowers, of all take an equal amount; and grind, and make into a paste with salty water or plain water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place any plaster on a broken limb to restore it but only a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderately warm and not too hard or too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen also recommends that one should apply to a broken limb, for the purpose of restoring it, mildly warm dry substances such as myrrh, aloe and incense, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is useful for wound and pain: take a beetle and chopped off human hair or bird feathers, and red lead, and boil evenly, and grind, and make it into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place; if so, do not loosen it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, soaked in water, and lift the area, until the itching stops and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool on it, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it to a cushion until you are sure that the abscess is hot.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then gently restart the dressing, and a little poultice, and do not constrict it as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful and has drained completely, and you need a poultice and bandage, then reapply it as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if there is no improvement in the limb after what we have said, do not loosen it for three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, until the break heals, and bring the joining closer to the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then bind it more tightly than before and fatten the flesh as I said earlier; and if you see that the area dries out more than necessary, know that there will be no healing.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	boil the joint in hot water each time you release it, every third day, and loosen the ligament a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	therefore cutting off the blood supply to the limb through this procedure will quickly correct the harm caused by foolish surgeons who incorrectly reset the limb; this is dangerous, and I see no other option but to stop and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	on various types of fractures.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with different shapes and causes;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by sword blows that cut the bone all the way down to the shaft below it, similar to what a hatchet or stick does, and this type of fracture is called "haichure".[ITA]
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a hidden impact, or a crack from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone or is on top of it, and this wound is either large or small.[Note: "toile" in Old French can mean "membrane", "fabric", or "canopy". In this context, it likely refers to the membrane (periosteum) that covers the surface of bones. The translator had to make a judgement call on this one.]
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound lodged in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "hairline".[Note: The Old French word "chevous" means "hairs", but can also refer to any thin or fine object. Here, it likely refers to hairs, hence the translation.]
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it drives the piece of bone inward, and the place is sunken in like blacksmiths do when they strike anvils; then stones enter inside.  [Note: The Old French word "chaudelier" can refer to various types of craftsmen who work with heated metal, but here it likely refers specifically to blacksmiths.][Note 2: I am not sure if my translation for "li leus chevez" is accurate; the phrase could also mean "the place is hairy", which doesn't make sense in this context. If anyone has a better suggestion, please let me know.]
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as the bones of children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs in all kinds of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the swelling on them, and through inquiry by touch, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top.[NOTE: I translated "char" as flesh since it can refer to any tissue in medical texts from this time period.]
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the fracture is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed over it, the fracture appears black.[NOTES: I translated "li brisure" as "the fracture," assuming that "brisure" is being used as a noun here. Also, I translated "capillaire" as "appearance" since this word can mean several things including hair-like or relating to the head.]
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of any adverse symptoms in the patient, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, pallor, fever, and redness and protrusion of the eyes, among other things in various conditions; for without doubt, it cannot heal if these are present.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, you should quickly remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth underneath the bone does not become rotten, and the accidents that we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break of the bone reaches to the cloth that covers the brain, then you must cut open the split part in this way: by taking the patient's head and uncovering the bone as much as you can, and on the surface of the wound as gently as you can,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the flow of blood comes when you uncover the bone, or there is an abscess coming, then you should help with what is necessary and that is to fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil.[Reformatted for readability]
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscess has calmed down, and you are assured of proper blood flow; then begin along the bone to remove, and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and this is the method:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision, larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the flesh.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, then you must drill around it so that you provide cuts with terraces (ledges), not going through the bone but stopping at the outer layer of the bone, leaving a margin or circle on the tip that does not allow the tip to go beyond the bone; and you will need several of these, so that each one comes into place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have terraces for all parts of the bone; and this is the method of the three types of terracing:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a awl on the bone, and turn to your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further, and do so all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as tongs, pliers; and make sure that you do not touch the brain or the sutures.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and pulled out the bone, it is necessary to insert an instrument that resembles a knife but must be more slender and finer than the other knives;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains any small bones or shards, gently remove them with an instrument; then clean the wound of pus and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is as described by Galen, which is safer, and he highly recommends it; here is what he says:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. Once you have uncovered this area, place beneath the tip of this lunate knife, of which the shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not saw in one direction, but rather make the cut on two sides, so that the knife faces the bone. Then strike it lightly with a small mallet, cutting through the bone all the way around, taking great care not to damage the tissue beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhered to the bone, carefully detach it, for it can be removed without causing harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the periosteum (the membrane covering the bone), but rather is only cut from above with fragments remaining, then you must smooth over this roughness and remove the small flakes using a sharp razor, which you should have in various sizes, so that you can choose the most suitable one for each situation depending on the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king before large razors, and afterward with more fine ones, and do not stop until it is fully done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other case of hair trimming and fine bone breaking, it is necessary to arrange the direction accordingly; and this is not an easy task even for those who have devoted their studies to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the abscess is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound, soak it in rose oil and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another double-layered cloth and soak it in wine and rose oil and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as gently as possible to avoid causing further harm, then place a bandage over it without tightening it too much, just enough to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has subsided, then loosen it and apply medicine, such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, and continue to administer painless medicine.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and make sure that the wound stays clean, not allowing any residue to remain, nor letting pus gather, because when pus forms on the covering of the brain, it will eat away at it and cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on top of the siphac (a medical term used in this text), it causes necrosis.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any adverse event befalls the patient, as we have said, there is reason for doubt and fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other cause of blackening is present but from the medicine that has been applied, which may have such a power, then take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, mix it with one cloth, and place it on the siphac (a medical term used in this text).[ST1]
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with various treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break but only becomes swollen or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or the nostril's opening into the break, and push it back into place with your index finger, until the nose regains its natural shape.[*]
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, taking care that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your finger cannot reach it, you should use a small piece of wood to push it back into place.[*]
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, make it like new again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you are able;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then apply a bandage of linen cloth to the swelling if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or place one [bandage] on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be thick enough to fill the openings of the nose.[source_author](Guido of Arezzo)
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that one should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day. This does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened in the preparation of egg white and powdered mold; then leave the bandage until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose instead of bandages, with a soft cloth around it, and this holds the fracture together, and the patient blows through it; do what you will.[source\_author](Guido of Arezzo)
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pustulent abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put either cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a piece of lily root.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if no abscess comes, put an emplaster on the outside, made of chamomile flour and powdered incense, congealed with egg white, then place light wicks on top, but do not bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break of the nose is small and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound and cure it of foreign matter and dead flesh, and suture it, using appropriate plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then cure it with bandages and put in splints of wood until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	about the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is not present but only a protrusion inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture back into place, and align it with the other hand from the outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two parts, you must apply extension to both parts until they are aligned.[df-note] Note: I translated "desevree" as "separated" and "extension" as "applied force to stretch or extend a part of the body."
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or a fracture, then bind them with a golden or silver or silk thread, and apply a cerate on the broken jaw, and place a double bandage over it. Place a large well-made star-shaped object or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up high on the head as tightly as possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has become misaligned; and apply a plaster on top, with powder from the mill and plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and place light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it is healed; it is often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound at the same time, see if any piece of bone has been removed from it; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.[Read More](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as necessary.[Read More](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)[ ](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of appropriate plasters to it, to help heal the flesh, until it has healed.
de la forcele	The word "de la forcele" does not appear in the provided text. If you could provide more context or the full sentence, I would be happy to help translate it.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks in several places before the shoulder, and there are three types of fractures: one where it is broken and dislocated in two pieces, which is easier to reset; and another with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is as follows when the fracture is without a wound: that you have two assistants, one holding the injured collarbone and the other extending the neck towards the side; then place the break between your hands so that it is in its proper shape and there is no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder and make it thick as needed; then extend and lift the collarbone and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you can place the break in its proper position.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus outward because it is deep within, an oversized pillow should be placed under the patient's shoulder blade, and the assistant should push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then realign the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you should cut open the wound further; gently pull out the fragments and, if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, saw one of the ends of the bone that is causing the obstruction. But make sure to place the instrument called a "syfac" under the humerus to protect it.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should resemble a spoon, but not have a handle, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the demands of the task. It should have two openings, one large and one small, similar in shape to the wound you made when pulling out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain that a hot abscess has formed, cut open the wound, and if the opening is small or there is uncertainty whether it is a hot abscess, pack the wound with cloth and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, wet a dressing in rose oil, vinegar, and assyl (a type of resin), and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The squeezing of the bone, when it is without wounds and without a surgeon, is to put powdered plaster and egg white on the bone, and place light wicks on top, and place a stick underneath the pelvis if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then place a double cloth on the wicks and the plaster; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, leaving the ends of the bandage hanging.[5](https://futurism.media/api/v1/website/link/ba67fb4e-dc3e-4c0d-8e2b-db87eb90bc01)
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And place the stick on the fracture, then wrap the bandage around the neck and under the healthy and affected pelvis; and rub it on each part, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the binding loosens, tighten it again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under their shoulder blade to lift the upper part; this will lighten the fracture of the collarbone through the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an adverse event occurs, for up to 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the poultice if necessary, and keep it on while it heals, until they are restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of a shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It often happens that a broken or dislocated shoulder is not visible externally, and can only be detected through touch; in this case, treat it according to the type of fracture, resetting it to its natural shape in every way possible; then put powdered flour with egg yolk, light bandages, and a double cloth on top; next place a broad, thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate, fill them with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then secure it firmly with a large bandage, making sure that the plate does not move from its position, and check the binding daily; and tighten it every time it loosens, and adjust the plate if it moves from its position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this period is over, release it, but be careful, as it is not an easy task to keep the bone in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not underneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut it as we have said in the break of the forearm to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the break of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone can sometimes break in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks near the joint. And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of strength, and may even vomit blood, and there is a noticeable indentation in the broken bone, which can be felt.[
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration process is as follows: the patient lies down on their back, and a cushion is placed between their shoulders. Then, the shoulders are pressed together, and the ribcage is pulled inward with both hands, gently and carefully equalizing the alignment of the broken bone as much as possible, until the shape of the bone is correct. After that, ointments and compresses are applied on top of a thin layer of salt or other light wood, then wrapped in a bandage and tied over the broken bone so that it does not move. The bandage is wrapped around the back and tightened appropriately, and re-tightened every hour if it loosens. If it becomes necessary to loosen the bandages due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, then do so immediately, remove the ointment, treat the affected area, reapply the ointment, and rewrap the bandage tightly until healed.[
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination of the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the setting of the break is thus: align the fracture as it should be. Then apply a plaster and bind it with a bandage if you have need of one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the rib is angled inward, then the patient feels great pain and a stitching sensation, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the flesh; and the lung has prickly points, and soon vomits up large quantities of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have applied much skill to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one must administer foods which cause the belly to swell, in order to push the break outward.[Note: This suggests that the recommended diet is intended to increase gastric distension and thereby help realign the broken ribs.]
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come to a boil, then lance them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece. And some of you have said that the place should be covered with a cloth soaked in warm oil and then bandages should be placed between the ribs to evenly distribute pressure around it, and then treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food and medicine.

And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pointing through the cloth, and there is fear for the patient, then you must cut on the place of the broken rib, and place a tool underneath to protect the lung; and then you should saw the bone and gently remove it, and then sew up the two sides of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals. de la brisure dou col	of the breaking/fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a breaking/fracture of the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shin bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight reduction in size at the end; it becomes long, deviates to the side, and causes pain to the patient at the site, as well as bruising and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand upon it, until you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the top only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.

And if the break is long or it slants inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that break is clear to you.

And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice and place a stick or bone splint on top of it, holding the break in place so that it does not move; and fill the space beneath with a pad, until the area is even
