And if abscesses come there, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and use what we mentioned before; then return to the restoration, holding it in place as is necessary, unless there is an adverse event; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the part between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored in one of two ways: the first way is to take a stick of medium size, shaped as follows:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two arms with two bandages and pull them upwards, and seat the patient on a chair; then lay his dislocated arm over the stick so that it rests in the middle of the stick, forming an arch; then hang a heavy weight or have the assistant stretch it downward; then place the healer's hands around the fracture, bringing the ends of the fracture together until the broken bone returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to lay the patient on his back with his dislocated arm raised upwards and tie his hand to his neck; then command two assistants, one takes hold of what is above the fracture with both hands, and the other holds it below with a bandage, extending each one in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you feel that the extraction is too strong, tighten one bandage above and below the fracture and have each assistant pull in their direction. And if the fracture is close to the top of the shoulder, place one bandage beneath the armpit and another near the neck, beneath the fracture; and similarly, if the fracture is towards the side, place a light bandage without effort so that the fracture is aligned properly over the socket and the upper arm; then align the fracture as it should be and tighten it, if there are no abscesses present.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses appear, do not bind it until 7 days have passed, and put a damp linen cloth on it, soaked in oil of roses, until the abscess has calmed down; then bind it, and the method for binding is to put the poultice on the armpit, then place the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put the cloth, and bind on the armpit, and on the arm, so that the arm stays in place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bones are not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bone is broken, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the break than the others, and have one finger space between each splint, and let each splint be so big that it extends beyond the break by three fingers on each side; then bind on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more tightly and less loosely, on the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the positioning and binding of the splints, as we have said, at the time that you reset the broken member, and you are unsure whether an abscess is present, then leave it to bind for seven days, as we have said; then look at the bandage every three days, to see if there is itching or swelling or redness appearing where pus cannot come to the member because the binding is too tight. If so, adjust it as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, do not loosen it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back and have their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of equal wool underneath the armpit, and check every hour during the day or night that the position of the broken member does not change or that the binding has not become loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give them the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at first subtle; and when they begin to recover, let it be thick. And it is customary for the armpit and leg to regain strength in 40 days; and then one should unbind and administer baths and medicinal ointments to heal the wound. And if the binding is tight and swollen, then delay unbinding for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of 2 bones, which are called the "humerus", one of which is small, and it is this one that follows the armpit; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps the large humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small humerus is broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult and worse than when both are broken together. If it is only the small humerus that is broken, then it should be slightly extended and put in a straight position.[5](https://medicalterms.co/what-does-humerus-mean/)
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then it must be stretched more forcefully and laid out on a cushion. The patient's arm should be positioned with the armpit higher than the rest of the body, and the little finger lower than the other fingers. The patient should be cross-wise on the cushion, with another cushion raised in front of them so that they are comfortable and not in any pain. Then, the minister should extend the broken arm below, either using a bandage or some other support. Another minister should support the uninjured arm above. The surgeon should then align the broken bone as well as possible.[5](https://medicalterms.co/what-does-humerus-mean/)
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the break is in pieces, then each piece should be put in its place. And if there is any fragment that pierces the heart and cannot be restored to its place, then a hole must be made through the ribs and the fragment removed, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, which I have spoken of in a previous chapter, then attend to the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the healing process, abscesses occur, then take a cloth covered in a mixture of rose oil and white wax that is not too hard or soft; and place a cloth gently over it until the abscess has calmed down. Then remove the cloth and apply a plaster made of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg whites, then apply the splints, and let the splint for the fracture be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that there should be six splints on the arm in multiple arrangements: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two; and bind more firmly above the fracture than elsewhere, always lessening tension as time goes on, as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread used for binding be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And observe the member and the bandage after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that occurs on the member, then you must rinse the member with warm water until the itching has calmed down; and let the member rest without being tightly bound. Then reapply the binding, and if the bindings have loosened and the bones have become separated or something similar, then fix it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the swelling cannot reach the member because it is too tightly bound, then loosen it slightly and leave it like that for several days until the swelling returns, and then rebind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have mentioned occur to the patient, do not release it for forty days or thereabouts; then bind his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and beware of movement and loosening, and let him sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Here is the translation of the given Old French sentence into modern English:
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles of the fingers are rare, and only swelling comes there often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, then the patient should sit cross-legged and face straight ahead evenly; then place his hand on a spread-out cloth, and have the assistant extend the broken bones, and align them properly so that they are well joined; and apply a dressing and bandages, unless pus forms, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the breaker is around the belly of the sole, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken sole; and then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and let the stick be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is above, then you must place a stick on top of it, and another below in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and make the binding tight between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our fingers, if it is the thumb, then set it straight as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit, place a small straight stick on top to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in one of the other fingers, such as the index or another, then set it straight and bind it with the good finger that follows it; or bind them all together, which is easier, or place a stick on top, like with the thumb; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and help those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Here is the translation of the text you provided: "of the broken thigh" or "of the thigh that has been fractured."
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and this is easily seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one bandage is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends their bandage to their equal part; and this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, then one of the bandages should be towards the wrist, and the other below the break. And likewise if it is close to the knee, and then the bandage should be next to the knee, and the extension downwards; then the surgeon places the bone even with his two hands, until it is in its natural shape, and then applies the poultice, and binds it, if pustules do not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the binding is done in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the break a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let the excess hang down; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread to above; then turn around the leg and thigh the bandage, then put on the break supports, and put a support on the bone of the leg; then fill the gap between the thigh and the leg with soft rags to apply equal tension, then begin to bind firmly three or four turns on the break; and when it goes above the break, tighten less; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three supports that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, so that it comes next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, unless there comes an abscess or swelling or any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen it, and realign what is out of place, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of bone that prick, they must be gouged out if possible; and if not, the place must be split open and drawn forth; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that splints are placed in it, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in this type of restoration, the patient does not fare well.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or less or more, depending on the differences in constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there often occurs a small break, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and this happens with all wounds, with or without wound, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that you set even what is dislocated at its ends, until it can be moved again; then apply the poultice and place a round bandage if necessary, and bind it as needed. Then consider all the precautions we have mentioned in other breaks, such as hot abscess and others; and for each symptom do what is necessary, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	about the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called by its right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it has all kinds of fractures just like in the arm, and therefore the restoration is also similar to that of the arm, and the work is exactly the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, the leg bends in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it is visible; it bends downwards. Then provide extension, align it straight, and bind the ends evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is severe and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; and raise it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two rods of stripped wood that extend along the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and bind it in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and this is good. And some administer a splint as long as the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly in fractures where there is a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is any inflammation or other accident; and care for it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but sometimes there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and the toes, and it only results in a crush injury in multiple ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see the bones sticking out over each other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are protruding, press it firmly until they return to their place, then apply a plaster and bandages, and place a small board with two flat pieces under the affected foot, then bind it to the foot with bandages and any other necessary materials.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding because you will find that the bones are even, whether they were fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are fractured, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken toe according to the length of the toe, and make it slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned earlier, and bind it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, fractured toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it be placed on top of the chief (top surface) of the board outside the belly of the foot, so that it touches it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and treat each incident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Here is a line-by-line translation of the provided Old French text:
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature (genital area) is broken, make her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back and support her from behind; fill a bowl with cotton and place it under her genitals, making sure it is as thick as a finger; then stand the woman up, lift her hips, and let the cotton come out of her genitals until it reaches the broken bone, which will be drawn back into place by the finger-thick cotton; when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton and replace it after she finishes; do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be healed. If you wish, take a bladder of animal intestines, attach a cane to its opening, insert the entire bladder into her genitals, then blow forcefully through the cane until the bladder is filled inside; this will bring the broken bone back together; then fill it with cotton and leave it for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the forearm bone of a man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have described for the thigh bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who study and practice this art, and pay attention to my book. For fractures indicate in various ways the correct path to restoration, so understand that.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis in it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, just as the drainages that we have mentioned testify to.[note]Here, "sainies" refers to the drainage or discharge from the wound, indicating its healing progress. The translator has chosen to use the word "testify" to convey the idea that these drainages provide evidence of the healing process. However, this is a somewhat loose interpretation and other possible translations include "show", "indicate", or simply "are".[/note]
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then cauterize it with vitriol if you have nothing else, then begin to heal the fracture in that same hour or on that day, unless abscesses come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses arise there, then leave the healing until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would cause a harmful incident to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin, it is necessary to put it back in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to put it equal with your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, with 7 or 8 holes that are long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare 3 or 4 (finger) rings, depending on what is needed in each bone-breaking cure; and let them be round and a little thick, so that they do not bend during compression on the member while you are working, and let it be sharp at the front, and thick from the middle to the end, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "palancelle," for which reason the curved part must be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it once, until it becomes aligned, and let them be even with each other. And if the fracture is delicate and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you should cut the end of the bone, so that the instrument has enough power to do its job.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot set the bone as we have described, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as a knife or scalpel, to your best ability; then smooth down any roughness and small shards left in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is set back in place and the patient still feels great pain, know that it is not yet in its natural position. Make sure it is in its proper place, then wet a cloth in black stiptic wine, and apply it properly if it is summer; and do not put any ointment or other things with oil on the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer painkillers when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the break; for many foolish surgeons have done this, causing the patient either death or corruption; and let the restraint be softer and milder than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is large or deep, and you fear that some mishap may occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then it is not appropriate to apply painkillers; instead, wrap around it, in place of painkillers, hard cloths and bind them. And when you see after one day or two that pus has formed on the wound, remove what you have applied and replace it with a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it has healed and become clean.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be arranged in such a way that pus drains away easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days they are beyond repair, and it can no longer join but keeps bowing back, know that there are small fragments of bone, therefore you need to stitch the wound with sutures, and remove all the separated pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you must treat it, according to what is stated in its chapter earlier. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the leg bone or the shoulder blade, and others similar to the large members, then do not pull it out, because many times death ensues, but instead leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come upon sutures
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across this after the healing of a fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it is an unpleasant sight to see the appearance of the member; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take great care then if it is fresh to us: and administer styptic medicines to him, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollex, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg yolk or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in wicks, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen, and begin another, until the knots are removed; or you strain on a piece of wood well made; for the property of wood is that it removes all swelling above the members; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess appear; or you have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weak member after healing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the member remains weak and fragile afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to an excess of moisture; or due to excessive movement, not at the appropriate time; or because there is little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths for him, and give him joy and pleasure; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish ones who say that the limb should be broken again; many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and cause great harm, and perhaps even death; nevertheless, if the knots and tension are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as vismalve leaves and roots, melilot, and similar things; and make a softening poultice, such as a well-made diaclytic, and take the mucilage of vismalve and thicken it with chicken fat or oil of Saint John's wort, and make a poultice; or take greasy figs, and crush them with dung from a horse, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the knots are removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. And gentle movement should be restored to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with a iron, then it should be covered down to the bone with a sharp incision made with a delicate lancet; and cotton and a bandage should be used in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one waits, the area swells, and there is a risk that it cannot be returned to its proper place; therefore, it must not be moved at the time when it is swollen, as this often brings on spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this occurs, let the patient be bled, then allow them to rest until the abscess has subsided; then apply warm water and oil to the affected limb, gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the limbs from head to feet.
des mandibules	of the jaw(s)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the jaws are dislocated on both sides, and there are two ways in which dislocation of both occurs: either they are slightly out of place and somewhat loose; or they are completely dislocated and hang toward the back, and saliva flows from the mouth that he cannot hold in, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue becomes entangled as he speaks.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its place through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and full, then you must quickly reset it and not delay at all;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and with one of his hands places his thumb into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-parted; and let him place the other hand outside to adjust evenly; and command the patient to relax and move his jaw in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician adjusts it evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it's both jaws together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can easily adjust them; do not delay in readjusting, as we have said.[Notes:
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are evenly readjusted and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, then place dampened cloths soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on it, and bind it lightly with soft ligatures.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, with his heels resting between two cushions, so that they are not moved to the right or left, and do not strain to move, but eat light food until the pains are eased, and the jaw muscles are relaxed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then eat what they want lightly, and do not strain to open their mouth while eating and drinking, until the jaw muscles are relaxed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be restored to their place in an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fevers and habitual swelling may follow, and possibly abdominal distension, and perhaps vomiting of bile.[ ](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/pur)
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a lost cause; and many times, those to whom it happens die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork/fracture/dislocation
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot be removed from the side towards the back and the hip, and it is dislocated at times to the outside, which can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the reduction is as follows: let the patient lie down on their back, extend their arms, then press firmly with your palm on the affected area, and it will return to its place; then apply a plaster and bandage, and bind it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the head that is turned towards the ribs cannot be dislocated; if it can, and if it has been dislocated once, then reset it in its place as we have said; then apply a plaster and bandage, and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed.[IT] Translate this Old French text into English:
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the head of the shoulder blade is reset when it has become dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways only: one of which occurs when it dislocates at the part of the socket underneath; the second, when it dislocates at the part of the hip; and it may also happen to dislocate at the top part, but this is rare.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it should never dislocate backwards at the shoulder, nor dislocate inwards towards the nerves; and more often than not, it dislocates downward towards the socket, especially for those who have little flesh, as it easily slips out; but for those who have enough flesh, it takes longer to slip out and also takes longer to return.[5]
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it may happen to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, causing the shoulder to swell from a hot abscess, and they mistakenly believe that it is dislocated because of this.[5][1](Ch. 23)
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.[5][1](Ch. 23)
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it moves down towards the shoulder blade, and it creates a noticeable difference between the healthy and diseased shoulder.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder blade touching the top of the shoulder as if it were an egg, and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, as you can clearly feel it by touching.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place when it is new or if the child is sick.[INTRODUCTION] Welcome to the medieval medical translation series! Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the servant raises the patient's hand up high, then puts your fingers underneath the joint, and forcefully lifts the joint up to its place; and the servant lifts the hand, stretches it up, then puts it down; and it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said many days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and an easing and soothing aroma should be administered to them, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and they should be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then let the patient be propped up on their back, and place a woolen support underneath the joint, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the patient's heel on the support, and lift the shoulder blade forcefully, and pull the affected limb.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And let another servant hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to reset it in this manner.
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and make sure there is a person present who is bigger than the patient; and they should stand to the patient's side, and push their shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the edge of the bed upwards, so that the patient is hanging in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and have another assistant pull the patient's hand down towards the stomach. And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold onto something heavy, and the dislocation should return to its proper position now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it can also be reset in another way, by inserting a long stake into the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is as round as a fist, and neither too thick nor too thin.[5]
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	and place it underneath the patient, but make sure there are soft blankets on top of them, and have the patient lie down lengthwise along the stake. Then stretch out their hand away from the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its proper position.[5][References edited for brevity.]
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not want to return despite all the things we have said, perform this treatment: take a stick of 2 arms' length and 4 fingers' width, which has a rounded head to easily enter deep beneath the dislocation, in the following form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	place a soft cloth over the patient's head, so that the stick does not hurt or wound them, then place it beneath the dislocation of the patient; stretch the arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder of appropriate width, and let the hand hang down, leaving the body suspended on the other side: now the joint will return to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should put a pad of wool of equal size under the dislocation, then apply a poultice made with powdered flour, incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it, then tie it in place beneath the dislocation, and turn the bandage over the poultice, and hold the hand to the neck, leaving the hand remaining in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat only soft food until the limb is healed, as this will promote faster healing; and then eat normally after 5 or 7 days, and move the limb; and if it feels firm and not swollen, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries to it at three points, as it is stated before in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be raised, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never return to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation that is towards the side of the buttocks or the back is made by a thrust and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a substitute; and care should be taken until it has healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracking in the limb and slow movement, then the patient should use baths many times until that cracking is eased and returns to its original state.[Machine translation](Note: The following translations were generated by machine translation services and may contain errors.
