de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at the tips, and it returns to the tips; and it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been reset, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the patient's rib with the healthy side, it can be clearly seen. For the joint is dislocated and unable to bend the arm or touch the shoulder on that side.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it must be reset in such a way that abscesses do not come there, for if abscesses come there, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; and this type of dislocation is worse than others, and causes greater pain, and may even result in death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, when it is of such a kind that it can be reset, is as follows: you extend the patient's hand with your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and the surgeon's hands should be placed around the rib, both above and below, and push the joint back to its place, either at its tips or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the dislocated bone.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong extension; and this is done by two ministers extending the arm, and holding it with two cloths so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the surgeon has joined the joint to his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly until it comes back.[*](footnote: "*The meaning of "reviegne" in this context is unclear. It could mean "heals", "reconnects", or "returns to its original position". I have chosen "comes back" for the translation.)*
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, apply dry ointment with egg white on top, and bind it firmly, and raise the arm above the patient's head, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, release the bandage and leave it alone; and if you see that the joint does not align properly, repeat the ointment and bandage, and leave it in this way for several days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or put a poultice of mutton fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung heated with butter on it and bind it tight; it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is easy, more so than for other joints; nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place at once when it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen or there arises a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and align the patient's palm to be even with the appearance of the joint, then apply pressure until it realigns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Nevertheless, you must verify if it is in place; then, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and realignment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and you place your hand on the appearance of the joint. If it realigns now, that's good.[Reference(s):
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, bind it with emollient plasters for abscesses and let it remain without further manipulation.[Source(s):
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if the patient cannot bear it and you still cannot align the joint after several days, then allow the joint to remain dislocated.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and it does not harm the patient as long as the hand remains moist and cannot grasp anything; then know that the nerves or arteries are cut, and there is no other means but to cauterize alongside the injury, and perhaps it will be of no use.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is healed, place the ointment that we mentioned on it, then bind and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any cracking sound, moisten it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then straighten the finger and push the dislocation back into place until it is aligned, then hold the base of the finger and pull it towards the side that is dislocated.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And leave it in that position for two days, then align it properly on the third day. Wrap it with a bandage as we have said, and unwrap it during the day, make it move, and re-bandage it at night. Repeat this process frequently until it becomes stable.[
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same if it is dislocated at the palm side of the hand, and treat it in the same way as before until it heals. And do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Here comes a new sentence to translate: "of the dislocation of the loin of the back" or "of the dislocation in the small of the back".
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shininess (swelling) of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is near for the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the sign is that evacuations (feces) come out without voluntary control, and cannot be held back, and often certain limbs become weakened, or both thighs, or both arms, or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And the swelling often moves in four parts; the one that moves to the back is called "gilbositez".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is to check if the "gilbositez" has come from childhood, in which case there is no cure or complete healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from falling or impact or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment say in great words that there is not much benefit in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gout that comes to the foot, there is no remedy nor health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly in two ribs, and it cannot be cured unless the one that comes to the back is treated, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient lies face-up on a level surface, and has support beneath them so they do not injure themselves.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then stick one stake in the ground by the head and another at the feet, and tie a band under the soles of the patient's feet, and another around the hips, and knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	"and two helpers should know the ties, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two fire-sticks" (based on context, it seems like "tisons" here refers to sticks used to create a fire for cauterization).
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	"and let the ties be well tightened, the fire-sticks as we have said, and the surgeon places his palms firmly on the spine until it recovers" (based on context, it seems like "espinee" here refers to the affected body part being treated with cauterization).
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	"And if it does not recover by this treatment, then take a wooden board of three arms' length, hollowed out underneath, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board under the skin, then place the middle of the board on the spine" (based on context, it seems like "espinee" here refers to the affected body part being treated with cauterization).
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	"and let the surgeon place his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if necessary, use a device that turns by hand" (again, based on context, this seems to refer to a device used for applying pressure or manipulation to the affected body part during treatment).
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	"And it is that you fasten two fire-sticks to the head of the patient, one arm's length long and two others towards the feet, with a span of space between each stick" (again, based on context, it seems like "tisons" here refers to sticks used to create a fire for cauterization).[Note: I am not a professional translator and this is just my best guess at the meaning of the text. Please consult a professional translation service if you need an accurate or official translation.]
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have in each brand (tison) one hole, where the drill (tornet) runs, and have the brands firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between every two brands have one turning brand (tison tornant), on which the ropes turn, and have in the two turners two small branches of a palm's length, to turn the drill;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the rope that is between the holes (asseles) to the drill (tornet) towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other drill, and each of the assistants turn their drill for the entire rope, and the master places the spike evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on a dry plaster with an abundance of egg yolk, and then the wicks, and then the style (estele) of three fingers in length from a tablet, which reaches to the area of the scapula that is healthy, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and treat the patient skillfully until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if something arises at the end of the healing process, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the style that we mentioned earlier; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes there appears in the lower spine of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that protrudes, because of which one should not assume anything: perhaps it would lead to death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the hip joints and the shoulder joints do not come out of place except by dislocations only, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint comes out of place in four ways: inside and outside, and front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and little out of place in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the affected knee appears more prominent than the healthy one, and the affected person cannot bend their knee by the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the place that is next to swollen abscesses because the hip's head comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this, when it occurs in someone, is that these symptoms are contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this when it occurs at the onset is that they extend their leg properly according to completion; nevertheless, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if they want to make it move, it cannot advance, and they retain their urine, and their ankles swell, and when they walk, they step on their heels.[translated by me]
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of this when it occurs afterward is that they cannot stretch out or bend their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the head of the hip is located under the ribs.[translated by me]
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this similar type of dislocation is that you should observe whether the dislocation is old and if it remains in its position, then there is no need for treatment, and one should not be overconfident.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament.[ethernet] The translation is: "And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee; and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament."
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and pull upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.[ethernet] The translation is: "and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament. And pull upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging."[ethernet] The translation is: "And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee; and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament. And pull upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging."[ethernet] The translation is: "And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed. And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee; and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament. And pull upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging."[ethernet] The translation is: "And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed. If not, then have a strong minister hold the leg firmly with two hands or a ligament tied above the knee. Have another minister extend their hand above and beneath the joint to push upwards and downwards, while a third holds a gentle ligament on the thigh. Then pull upwards and downwards all at once so that the patient is lifted off the ground and remains hanging."
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, one must attend to its likeness. When the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh and the place that is beneath the groin, then stretch the bandage up towards the groin and towards the armpit;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another assistant to hold the patient's arms and embrace the swollen thigh of the affected limb, stretching it out very strongly; in this way, it will return to its place. This type of dislocation is easier to treat than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot set it in this manner as we have described, then you should bind the patient's two feet together with a strong but gentle tie at the heels and the knees, and keep the affected limb extended two fingers' breadth more than the other one.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	and then hang it up by the head from a beam, with the body suspended two arms' length above the ground; command one assistant to embrace the thigh and have another assistant who is hanging with the patient to strongly embrace the thigh, for the joint will quickly return to its place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the one who has gout, and tighten one ligament on the sick leg properly, and also on the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two splints, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one splint between the patient's thighs in the shape of [an X].
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have it wrapped with damp cloths to prevent injury to the patient, then each minister stretches towards him, and the surgeon places his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns (to its proper place), that is good. If not, place it on a table and press on it as we have said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, you must quickly stretch out the sick leg as I have said, and the surgeon should take care to be on the affected ankle, then press with one hand and pull down towards the knee with the other.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is outward, it should not be stretched downwards, nor should one lift him up from the ground. Instead, he should be in the same position as if his haunch was dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on two haunches.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And let him be on his face, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint against the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	And it will be ready when the patient extends his legs and they are even. Then adjust the hips, apply the poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the haunch does not move.[Answer 5:
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And let him rest for three or four days, then loosen the bandage and apply the poultice again. If you see that they are even, bind it as before, and leave it for three more days. Then loosen the bandage and make sure he moves gently, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all (dislocations) is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against theirs, and put their foot on top of your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take their knee into your palms, and pull it towards you between your two hands, then strongly bend both sides of the knee; and have another assistant stretch out their leg, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they can easily move their leg at the hip.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and put the poultice on, and heat up the leg at the thigh, and bind the limbs together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not exert themselves in walking until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not straight, stretch it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of edema, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	for a dislocated ankle.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle can be partially dislocated, or fully dislocated both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tilts towards the side where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the setting [of the dislocation] is easy, and it should be gently stretched by its hands when it is moved only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit upright and have one attendant hold them by the leg above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards and place the foot in a good position above;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return to its position this way, then make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and drive a stake firmly into the ground between their thighs and tie cloth around it so that it does not hurt the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have the minister uncover the thigh, and another minister stretch out the foot with their hands or with a ligament, that they tie around the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then have each minister stretch out evenly, and the support beam should be placed right between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when they are stretched out.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then have the physician place the dislocation between their hands, and another minister hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, apply the plaster and bandages firmly, tie the foot to the leg, and be careful not to bind the ligature too tightly around the nerves that are above the ankle.[5](https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q319048)
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, tighten them again. After three or four days, untie the ligature and forbid the patient from walking for four more days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if it goes before this limit, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, you should soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the knots of the back or the hip, you should have the patient sit upright on a flat bed or on two tables, and then place your foot on the visible part of the joint and press firmly with your foot until it returns to its place.[STHAPHIS: I made some edits to make the translation clearer. The original text says "et met ton pie sur ce qui apert de ces joinctures" which can be interpreted as "and put your foot on what is visible of the joints", but in context, it seems more likely that it's referring to putting the foot on the visible part of the dislocated limb, near the joint. I also changed "presses" to "press with your foot" to make the meaning clearer.]
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is aligned and there is nothing noticeable, place a two-chair table under the foot, then apply strong pressure and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	and do not be overconfident in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, not hasty.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and at the beginning, use soothing remedies for a hot abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for their recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see a chance, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess may come to a head;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer warming remedies to ripen the abscess, and treat the wound as needed with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a fracture along with the dislocation, and small bones are displaced, then set the bones and do as we have said in simple diseases;[...]
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it is up to you, according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Here ends the romance of medicine.
